 Aftab Alam, J. The appellant, Mohammed Ajmal Mohammad Amir Kasab Abu Mujahid (hereinafter referred to as the appellant or as Kasab), who is a Pakistani national, has earned for himself five death penalties and an equal number of life terms in prison for committing multiple crimes of a horrendous kind in this country.	Issue
Some of the major charges against him were conspiracy to wage war against the Government of India collecting arms with the intention of waging war against the Government of India waging and abetting the waging of war against the Government of India commission of terrorist acts criminal conspiracy to commit murder criminal conspiracy, common intention and abetment to commit murder committing murder of a number of persons attempt to murder with common intention criminal conspiracy and abetment abduction for murder robbery dacoity with an attempt to cause death or grievous hurt and causing explosions punishable under the Explosive Substance Act, 1908.	Facts
He was found guilty of all these charges besides many others and was awarded the death sentence on five counts, lifesentence on five other counts, as well as a number of relatively lighter sentences of imprisonment for the other offences.	Facts
Apart from the appellant, two other accused, namely Fahim Ansari and Sabauddin Ahamed, both Indian nationals, were also arraigned before the trial court and indicted on the same charges as the appellant.	Facts
At the end of the trial, however, the appellant was convicted and sentenced to death as noted above (vide judgment and order dated May 3/6, 2010 passed by the Addl.	Facts
Sessions Judge, Greater Mumbai in Sessions Case	Facts
No. 175 of 2009).	Facts
The other two accused were acquitted of all charges.	Facts
The trial court gave them the benefit of the doubt as regards the charges of conspiracy and abetment of other offences by conspiracy, and further held that the prosecution completely failed to establish those other charges that were made directly against them.	Facts
The judgment by the trial court gave rise to a reference to the Bombay High Court under Section 366 of the Code of Criminal Procedure (CrPC), registered as Confirmation Case No. 2 of 2010.	Facts
In addition to the reference, two appeals also came to the High Court from the judgment and order passed by the trial court, one by the appellant against his conviction and sentences (Criminal Appeal No. 738 of 2010) and the other by the State of Maharashtra against the acquittal of the other two accused (Criminal Appeal No. 606 of 2010).	Facts
The High Court, by its judgment and order dated February 21, 2011, confirmed the death sentences given to the appellant by the trial court and dismissed both the appeals.	Facts
The High Court upheld the judgment and order passed by the trial court in all material aspects it sustained the appellants conviction and confirmed the punishments given him by the trial court, but at the same time it did not interfere with the acquittal of the other two accused.	Facts
From the judgment of the High Court two appeals have come to this Court one is a jail appeal by Kasab and the other is by the State of Maharashtra.	Facts
The States appeal seeks to challenge the acquittal of the other two accused by the trial court and affirmed by the High Court.	Facts
The other two accused are impleaded in the States appeal as Respondents No. 1 and 2.	Facts
Kasab was unrepresented in the appeal preferred by him from jail and this Court, therefore, appointed Mr. Raju Ramachandran, senior advocate, assisted by Mr. Gaurav Agrawal, to represent him.	Facts
He was thus able to get legal assistance of a standard and quality that is not available to a majority of Indian nationals approaching this Court against their conviction and sentence.	Facts
We may also state here that since it is a case of death sentence, we intend to examine the materials on record first hand, in accordance with the timehonoured practice of this Court, and come to our own conclusions on all issues of facts and law, unbound by the findings of the trial court and the High Court.	Facts
According to the prosecution, a sinister conspiracy was hatched in Pakistan and in furtherance of that conspiracy a savage attack was unleashed on Mumbai by a team of ten terrorists, including Kasab, who landed on the citys shores via the Arabian Sea.	Facts
The attack began on November 26, 2008 at about 9.15 PM and it ended when the last of the attackers, who was holed up in Hotel Taj Mahal Palace, was killed by Indian security forces at about 9.00 AM on November 29.	Facts
The brutal assault left Mumbai scarred and traumatized and the entire country shocked.	Facts
The terrorists killed one hundred and sixtysix (166) people and injured, often grievously, two hundred and thirtyeight (238) people.	Facts
The loss to property resulting from the terrorist attack was assessed at over Rupees one hundred and fifty crores (Rs. 150 Cr.).	Facts
The dead included eighteen (18) policemen and other security personnel and twentysix (26) foreign nationals.	Facts
The injured included thirtyseven (37) policemen and other security personnel and twentyone (21) foreign nationals.	Facts
Of those dead, at least seven (7) were killed by the appellant personally, seventytwo (72) were killed by him in furtherance of the common intention he shared with one Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) and the rest were victims of the conspiracy to which he was a party along with the nine (9) dead accused and thirtyfive (35) other accused who remain to be apprehended and brought to court.	None
The case of the prosecution is based, of course, on investigations by the police, but a good deal of it also comes from the confessional statement of the appellant recorded under Section 164 of the CrPC.	None
The confession of the appellant may be broadly divided into two parts, one relating to the conspiracy, planning and preparation for the attack, and the other relating to the actual attack on Mumbai, in execution of the conspiracy of which the appellant along with his buddia the accomplice Abu Ismail, was a part.	None
So far as the attack on Mumbai is concerned, every statement made by the appellant is corroborated over and over again by objective findings and evidences gathered by the prosecution.	None
But the conspiracy and the preparation for the attack took place in Pakistan and, therefore, it was impossible for any agency of this country to make investigations in regard to that part of the case.	None
Nevertheless, the investigators have been able to gather extensive material to corroborate even that part of the appellants confession.	None
It would thus be convenient to present the case of the prosecution by beginning with the appellants confessional statement.	None
THE RECORDING OF THE CONFESSIONAL STATEMENT The appellant was brought before the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Mumbai, on February 17, 2009, to make his confessional statement.	None
The Chief Metropolitan Magistrate referred him to Mrs. SawantWagule, Addl.	None
Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, 3rd Court, Esplanade, Mumbai, before whom he was presented for recording his confessional statement in CR No. 198/08 of Detection of Crime Branch, Mumbai (one of the twelve (12) cases registered in connection with the offences committed by the invading group of terrorists) at 10.45 AM on the same day.	None
Mrs. Sawant Wagule proceeded to take his statement very slowly and with great circumspection.	None
First of all, she had the appellant completely insulated from the police.	None
She explained to him that from that point he was in her custody and not in the custody of the police.	None
She asked him whether he was illtreated or abused by the police in any manner and why he wanted to make the confessional statement.	None
To her first question the appellant replied in the negative, and as for the reasons for him making a confession he said he would explain everything when his statement was recorded in detail.	None
The magistrate further satisfied herself that the appellant was willing to make the confessional statement voluntarily and not under any pressure, coercion or allurement by the police or anyone else.	None
Nonetheless, she did not take his statement on that day but told him that she wanted him to reflect further on the matter, for which purpose she was giving him 24 hours time.	None
She then remanded him to judicial custody where he was not accessible to the police or any other agency.	None
When the appellant was brought back to her on February 18 at 11 AM, she had another long exchange with him.	None
In the preliminary exchanges on the previous day she had found that the appellant had no difficulty in following or speaking in Hindi thus, the interaction between the magistrate and the appellant took place, in question and answer form, in simple, everyday spoken Hindi.	None
The magistrate, having satisfied herself that the police had no contact with the appellant in the past 24 hours, began by telling the appellant that she had no concern with the offences for which he was arrested or any connection with the police that had arrested him.	None
She explained to him that he was under no compulsion to make the confessional statement and further, that whether he made the confessional statement or not, he would not be handed back to the police.	None
She confirmed once again that the appellant wished to make the statement of his own volition and not under any influence.	None
The appellant told her his name and gave his address of a place in Pakistan.	None
She asked him about his education and where, when and how he was arrested by the police.	None
She asked him why was he brought to her and in reply he said that he wanted to make a confessional statement.	None
She asked for which offence he wanted to make confession.	None
He replied that on November 26, 2008, he and his accomplices made a Fidayeen attack on Mumbai city and he wanted to make a confession about the attack and the conspiracy behind it.	None
She asked when he felt like making a confession.	None
He told her that the thought of making the confession came to him when he was arrested by the police.	None
He added that he had absolutely no regret for whatever he had done.	None
He wanted to make the confession to set an example for others to become Fidayeen like him and follow him in his deeds.	None
The magistrate cautioned him by saying that he should make the statement only if he wished to do so.	None
She further cautioned him by saying that any confessional statement made by him would be taken down in writing and it would be used as evidence against him and that might lead to his conviction.	None
The appellant said he was aware of the consequences.	None
The magistrate again asked him whether the police had given any inducement to him to make the confessional statement, such as by offering to make him an approver.	None
He replied in the negative.	None
She then asked if he needed an advocate while making the confession.	None
Once again, he answered in the negative.	None
Even after this lengthy and detailed interaction, the learned magistrate did not take his confession on that day but gave him a period of 48 hours for further reflection, telling him that during that period he would not be in police custody but would be kept in jail in her custody.	None
She advised him to reconsider the matter with a composed mind.	None
She then remanded him to judicial custody with the direction that he be produced before her on February 20, 2009, at 11 AM.	None
The appellant was produced before the magistrate as directed, on February 20 at 10.40 AM.	None
The magistrate repeated the entire gamut of explanations and cautions at the end of which the appellant said that he still wanted to make his confession.	None
It was only then did the learned magistrate proceed to record the statement made by the appellant under Section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.	None
The statement could not be fully recorded on February 20 and it was resumed on February 21 at 10.40 AM.	None
On that date, the recording of the statement was completed.	None
The learned magistrate has maintained a meticulous record of the proceedings before her on all those dates, duly signed by the appellant.	None
After recording his statement, she also gave such certificates as required under subsection 4 of Section 164 CrPC.	None
Coming now to the main body of the confessional statement, it is in the form of a statement made by the appellant with only minimal interjections by the learned magistrate.	None
She occasionally asked the appellant to clarify the meaning of some uncommon words or code words used in the conspiracy.	None
The appellants statement, made before the magistrate over two days, is long and rambling, at points repetitive and full of seemingly superfluous details that would appear quite unnecessary if one is to take a limited view of the case and judge the culpability of the appellant only on the basis of the events in Mumbai.	None
To that end, it would be quite simple and convenient to give a brief summary of the appellants confessional statement.	None
But such an approach will not do justice to the case and we intend to take a look at the full statement of the appellant with all its repetitions and details.	None
We do so to be fair to both the prosecution and the appellant.	None
The details given by the appellant have a bearing on the prosecution case, according to which conspiracy, conspiracy to wage war against India and waging war against India are some of the main crimes in the case, and the details given by the appellant throw a great deal of light on the commission of those crimes.	None
Further, the details in the appellants statement are relevant to the submission that the confessional statement is not truly voluntary but that the appellant was manipulated into making that statement.	None
It is submitted on behalf of the appellant that no accused making an admission of his guilt would refer to those unnecessary details and that the great detail of the confessional statement only shows that it was not the appellant but the prosecution that was speaking through his mouth.	None
We, therefore, scan the confession as it is, in full, unabridged and unadorned.	None
THE KASAB NARRATIVE Family background The appellant started by giving his name as Mohammed Ajmal Mohammad Amir Kasab.	None
He was born on September 13, 1987.	None
He lived in Pakistan where his address was village Faridkot, tehsilDipalpur, district Okara, Punjab province, Pakistan.	None
He attended the Urdumedium Faridkot Government Primary School up to class 4.	None
He lived in the village with his Abbu Mohammad Amir Shaban Kasab, his Ammi NooreElahi, younger brother Munir and younger sister Surraiya.	None
He gave his fathers mobile phone number.	None
He had an elder sister and an elder brother, both of whom were married.	None
The sister lived with her husband at a village in Pathankot, district Okara, and the brother lived in Lahore with his wife.	None
He gave the names of the spouses of the elder sister and the elder brother and their respective addresses.	None
After the immediate family he gave the names of his three paternal uncles, elder to his father, and their sons, who lived in village Mohammad Yar Chishti, Pathankot, district Okara, Pakistan.	None
He also named a fourth paternal uncle, younger to his father, who lived with the appellants father.	None
He then gave the names of his Mamoon (mothers brother) and his three sons and a daughter and their address and the name of his Khaloo (mothers sisters husband), his address and mobile phone number.	None
He gave the name of another sister of his mother whom he called Mamo and her address.	None
He had two paternal aunts who were married.	None
He gave their names and their addresses.	None
He said that his Mamoon and Mousi (mothers brother and sister) had grownup children.	None
Kasab added that his house at Faridkot had been taken by his father who earned his livelihood by plying carts.	None
Kasab was fond of watching TV and Hindi movies he named a number of popular Indian films that he had seen many times.	None
He was in the habit of chewing tobacco.	None
He was good friends with the village doctor, Mazhar, who had a dispensary near Faridkot bus stop.	None
After dropping out of school in the year 2000, Kasab and his friend Dittu started working as labourers in Faridkot.	None
In 2001, he and his Abbu went to Lahore in search of employment.	None
In Lahore he lived with his father and uncle, Ghulam Rasool, in a house they rented from Haji Qamar.	None
He gave the detailed address of the house.	None
On his fathers instructions, Kasab started working as a labourer at Mazdooron Ka Adda.	None
He worked there for about five years.	None
In the year 2005, his father and uncle returned to their village.	None
Kasab continued to stay in Lahore alone, living in rented accommodation.	None
During this period he used to visit his village home.	None
On one such visit, he quarreled with his Abbu over the money earned by him.	None
After the quarrel he left the home and started living at Ali Hajveri Dargah in Lahore.	None
Kasabs friend Shafique got him a job in Welcome Tent Service.	None
He gave the full address of the establishment, the name of its owner and the mobile phone numbers of the owner and his son.	None
He added that the owner of the establishment used to call him Balka.	None
It was here that Kasab met and befriended Muzaffar Lal Khan, who also worked there.	None
Induction into LashkarEToiba, Indoctrination and Training for Jihad In November 2007, Kasab and Muzaffar Lal Khan went to Rawalpindi in search of better employment and took rented accommodation in Bangash Colony.	None
It was here, around the month of December, that they saw members of LashkareToiba going from door to door under the name of JamaatulDava, collecting hides of goats sacrificed on EiduzZoha.	None
They were asking people to donate the goat hides to help achieve independence for Kashmir.	None
Kasab and his friend developed great respect for those people.	None
They thought that those people were fighting for the liberation of Kashmir and they, too, should do something for their people.	None
When they were working at Sarai Alamgir members of JamatulDava were organising camps at different places where they would go to listen to their speeches.	None
He explained that after LashkareToiba was banned in 2002, it started its activities in the name of JamatulDava.	None
At this time, Kasab and Muzaffar Lal Khan first thought of undergoing training for Jihad.	None
In December 2007, they took the address of the office of LashkareToiba from a moulvi and reached its office at Raja Bazar, Rawalpindi.	None
He added that the office was near Bangash Colony.	None
There were two persons in the office who asked them the purpose of their visit.	None
They replied that they wanted to undertake Jihad.	None
The office people took their address in full and asked them to come the following day, with their clothes and other belongings.	None
They returned the following day.	None
On that day, a person in the office gave them a slip of paper with DauraESuffa, MarkazeToiba, Muridke written on it.	None
He gave them directions for Muridke and told them to go there.	None
They left for Muridke and, after traveling by bus for six hours, they reached Muridke bus stand.	None
From there, they walked for about a kilometer and a half to reach the camp site.	None
To the person there, they showed the letter and said that they had come for DauraeSuffa.	None
After subjecting them to a search, he took them inside the office.	None
There they showed the letter to a person called Fahadullah (wanted accused No. 8).	None
He wrote down their names and addresses and admitted them for the training.	None
DauraeSuffa training lasted twenty one (21) days.	None
There were thirty (30) other boys, apart from Kasab and his friend, doing the training.	None
During this, they were first converted from Sunni (sect of Islam) to AhleHadis and were given lessons in the Hadis (a study of the things said by the Prophet Muhammad and descriptions of his daily life).	None
An Ustad conducted physical exercises.	None
Besides, they were given lectures and lessons on Jihad.	None
In those sessions Fahadullah and Mufti Sayeed (wanted accused No. 13) were the Ustad.	None
The training took place between December 2007 and January 2008.	None
In the course of the training, Ustad Abu Kafa (wanted accused No. 5) introduced them to Hafiz Sayeed, the Ameer of LashkareToiba (wanted accused No. 1), Operational Commander ZakiurRehman Lakhvi (wanted accused No. 2), Area Commander Abu AlKama (wanted accused No. 4), Muzzamil alias Yusuf (wanted accused No. 6), Trainingincharge Abu Umar Sayeed (wanted accused No. 18) and Abu Hamza (wanted accused No. 3).	None
Kasab added that ZakiurRehman Lakhvi was known as Chacha and Lakhvi.	None
At that time Kafa told them that Abu Umar Sayeed arranged the training camps of LashkareToiba.	None
At this point the learned magistrate interrupted him to ask the meaning of the word Ameer.	None
He said it meant leader.	None
Kasab said that Ameer Hafiz Sayeed exhorted them by saying that all Mujahedeens must fight for the independence of Kashmir ZakiurRehman announced that the time had come for Jihad, adding that their orgainsation had been fighting in Kashmir for the last fifteen (15) years but the Hindustani Government was not allowing Kashmir to be independent.	None
It had, therefore, become necessary to fight a war against Hindustan to capture Kashmir.	None
ZakiurRehman Lakhvi asked them if they were ready to wage the war.	None
They all said they were ready for the war.	None
At that time, Abu AlKama told them that they had to attack the major cities of Hindustan that they would wage war against Hindustan from within, so that it is weakened from the inside.	None
He added that anyone who would die in this war would go to paradise.	None
In response, Kasab and all his associates said that they were ready to launch an attack on Hindustan.	None
In February 2008, they were selected for DauraeAmma training.	None
Ustad Fahadullah gave them a letter saying Bhai Vasool DauraeAmma, and sent them to Mansera Markaz Aksa.	None
They traveled for twelve (12) hours by bus to reach Mansera busstand from where they had to walk into the hilly region.	None
There, at the entrance to the camp they were subjected to a search.	None
They showed Fahadullahs note to the person at the gate and were allowed into the office.	None
The person in the office wrote down detailed information concerning them in a register.	None
After staying there for the day, they were taken to Buttel village in a van.	None
From there the driver of the van led them to the top of the hill on foot a walk of about thirty (30) minutes.	None
In this second training of twentyone (21) days they did physical exercises and practiced running and climbing over mountains.	None
They were also given training in dismantling and assembling Kalashan, rifles and pistols and taught how to fire these weapons.	None
Here the magistrate asked him the meaning of Kalashan.	None
He said Kalashan meant AK 47 rifle.	None
The Saving of Muzaffar During this training, Muzzafars elder brother came and took him from there.	None
Further Training Kasab told the magistrate that after the DauraeAmma training a Mujahid could go home if he so wished alternatively, he could remain for three months of Khidmat.	None
The magistrate asked him what Khidmat meant, to which he replied that it meant keeping watch on the new Mujahids who came for training, preparing food for them in the kitchen and generally looking after them.	None
He said that he remained to do Khidmat of the Mujahedeens.	None
The Ustad for the trainees who came there during Kasabs Khidmat were Abu Abdul Rehman (wanted accused No. 9), Yusuf (wanted accused No. 15), Abu Anas (wanted accused No. 10) and Abu Bashir (wanted accused No. 11).	None
Kasab did Khidmat during March, April and May, 2008.	None
Kasabs Ustad, Abu Abdul Rehman, then asked him to go along with the other Mujahedeens to the office of LashkareToiba at Model Town, District Okara for DauraeKhassa.	None
As instructed, they went to Mansera busstand in the LashkareToiba van.	None
After traveling from there by bus for twelve (12) hours they reached Lahore Lorry Adda (busstand).	None
From there they went to Okara busstand by bus and, after walking for about one kilometer, they reached the office of LashkareToiba near a Masjid at the corner of a lane in Model Town.	None
They told the people there that they had come to obtain the note for DauraeKhassa.	None
After making inquiries of them and after making verifications on the telephone, the person present there wrote a letter saying Bhai Vasool.	None
He stamped this with the flag of the LashkareToiba and gave it to them.	None
He also gave them the address of the LashkareToiba training camp at Muzzafarabad.	None
All of them travelled 16/17 hours in a bus to Muzzafarabad.	None
Kasab added that Muzzaffarabad is in POK.	None
From there they walked for about an hour and, passing through a LashkareToiba hospital called Neelam Dariya, they reached Sevai Nala.	None
At that place there were 10/12 houses and a masjid of LashkareToiba and the settlement was called Baitul Mujahedeen.	None
They gave the Rukka (chit) to a person called Sayeed and entered the training camp, which was also called Maskar Aksa.	None
The camp was situated on Chehalbandi Hills of Muzzaffarabad.	None
There was high security in this training camp and restrictions on moving in or out of the camp without the permission of the Ustad.	None
Abu Muavia (wanted accused No. 28) was the Ustad of this training, which was conducted in the months of May, June and July, 2008.	None
Kasab told the magistrate that this training was of two and a half months in course of which they were turned into solid Jihadis.	None
They were given lessons in Hadis, Namaz and Quran.	None
In addition, they were taught to dismantle and assemble Kalashans and many kinds of rifles and pistols, and to fire from those weapons, to operate rocket launchers and the use of hand grenades.	None
They were also given training in the use of satellite phones, GPS systems and mapreading.	None
The physical exercise comprised staying without food for 60 hours while climbing mountains with heavy loads on the back.	None
He added that the training was very arduous, so much so that ten (10) Mujahedeens fled the training camp.	None
Abu Muavia and Abu Hanzala (wanted accused No. 31) were the Ustad for this Daura.	None
During that training, a person unknown to Kasab visited the camp.	None
At that time, Ameer Hafiz Sayeed, ZakiUrRehman Lakhvi and Kafa were present there.	None
Ameer Hafiz Sayeed and ZakiUrRehman Lakhvi embraced the visitor, and Ustad Abu Muavia and Abu Hanzala saluted him in soldier style.	None
Kafa introduced him to the trainees as Major General Saab (wanted accused No. 20) adding that the persons who were giving them training were his men.	None
Major General Saab asked them their names and inquired about their training.	None
He asked whether they had any complaints.	None
They all answered that they had none.	None
Major General Saab left after talking to them for about an hour.	None
At this point, the magistrate asked Kasab for the name of Major General Saab.	None
He said they were not told his name Kasab said that after completion of the training his Ustad Muavia gave him Rupees one thousand and three hundred (Rs.1,300/) and asked him to go home and then to Ameer Hafiz Sayeeds office at Baitul Mujahedeen.	None
Preparation for attack on India Kasab stayed at his village for one week and then, towards the end of July, 2008, he reached the office of Hafiz Mohammad Sayeed at Baitul Mujahedeen.	None
From there Ustad Muavia took him to Selection Point at Sevai Nala, where 20/22 Mujahedeens like him were already present.	None
Also present were Ameer Hafiz Mohammad Sayeed, Muzammil, Abu Hamza, Ustad Muavia, Kafa and Abu AlKama.	None
The Mujahedeens were shown a CD on the laptop demonstrating how Salauddin had made a Fidayeen attack in Kashmir.	None
Thereafter, Abu AlKama explained to them in detail how Fidayeen attacks were made in Kashmir.	None
Ameer Hafiz Sayeed selected them and gave them new names.	None
He named Kasab Abu Mujahid and Imran Babar from Multan of Punjab region Abu Aqsa Nasir of Faisalabad was named Abu Umar and Nazir Ahmed Abu Omair Hafiz Arshad of Multan Road, Punjab, was called Abdul Rehman Bada alias Hayaji Abdul Rehman (Chhota) of Multan Road, Arabwala, was called Saqib Soheb from Narowala, Shakkar Garh, Punjab, was given the name Abu Soheb.	None
Some other colleagues of Kasab, who came from different places in Pakistan and whose names he did not recall but whom he identified with reference to the places from which they came, were similarly given pseudonyms by Hafiz Sayeed.	None
On the same day in the evening they were taken to the office of Baitul Mujahedeen.	None
The fifteen (15) selected persons then left for MarkazeToiba, Muridke, for the DauraeRibat training.	None
In this session, which lasted one month, they were given intelligence training, such as gathering knowledge about the target, keeping watch on him, following him and dodging if someone were to follow them.	None
Kasab described one of these tricks to the magistrate, telling her that if they suspected that they were being followed, they would switch on the indicator light on the right and then suddenly take a left turn.	None
That is how they would find out if they were being followed.	None
They learnt how to use fake identities while on a mission.	None
Training incharge Abu Sayeed gave special attention to this training.	None
He would frequently come to them and make queries about the training.	None
During the training two of Kasabs colleagues, Nasad and Abu Muavia, left the camp and went away.	None
Abu Kafa and Imran (wanted accused No. 12) were the Ustad of this Dauara.	None
During this training, Major General Saab came there twice.	None
He watched them train and encouraged them.	None
The Daura was completed in the end of August, 2008.	None
At that time Muzammil alias Yusuf and Abu AlKama had also come there.	None
Major Saab asked them if they could swim, to which they answered in the affirmative.	None
Then Major Saab asked Kafa to give them marine training.	None
Kafa said he would do so.	None
A few days later, in September, 2008, Kafa took them to Karachi by train.	None
There they were lodged in a house in Azizabad mohalla.	None
It was there in the month of September, 2008, that Ramzan started.	None
Kafa took all the thirteen (13) Mujahedeens to the creek from where they all sailed to the sea at Karachi on two small boats.	None
Here, they were put on a boat with an engine attached to it.	None
On that boat a person called Hakim Saab (wanted accused No. 14) gave them three days marine training.	None
During the marine training they were taught to read and use maps, to fathom the depths of the sea, to use GPS for marineways, to cast fishing nets and to sail.	None
At this point the magistrate asked Kasab why they were taught to cast fishing nets.	None
He replied that in order to deceive the naval officers of the enemy they would say they were fishermen.	None
After the marine training, Kafa took them back to Baitul Mujahedeen.	None
There, Ameer Hafiz Sayeed and ZakiurRehman Lakhvi asked them about the marine training.	None
Three days later, Ameer Hafiz Sayeed and ZakiurRehman Lakhvi sent six (6) Mujahedeens from among them (whose names Kasab told the magistrate) for a Fidayeen attack in Kashmir.	None
On the following day, Abu Hamza introduced three men to their group Ismail Khan from Dera Ismail Khan, Punjab, Fahadulla, and Javed from Okara, Punjab.	None
Hafiz Sayeed named them Abu Ismail, Abu Fahadullah and Abu Ali.	None
Abu Hamza told the group that these three were Fidayeens like them they had also taken training like them and they were also going with them to carry out the attack on Hindustan.	None
On the thirteenth (13th) Roza Hafiz Sayeed, ZakiurRehman Lakhvi, Muzammil alias Yusuf, Al Kama, Abu Hasan, Abu Kafa and Abu Umar Sayeed called them into the office of Baitul Mujahid.	None
Ameer Hafiz Sayeed addressed them there.	None
He said that the time for Jihad had come and they were now required to consider how best to launch the attack on Hindustan.	None
After him ZakiurRehman Lakhvi spoke and said that the economic strength of Hindustan lay in Bombay and it was therefore necessary to direct the attack on Bombay.	None

They saw a policeman coming.	None
Kasab pointed his Kalashan at him and fired, killing the policeman on the spot.	None
At that time they were fired at from the opposite direction.	None
They fired in retaliation and entered a lane.	None
They saw a white car with a red beacon light in the lane moving backwards.	None
Kasab fired at the car.	None
The car moved for a little distance and stopped.	None
Ismail threw a hand grenade at the car and Kasab again fired at it with a view to make the car move away from there.	None
But when they reached near the car and tried to open its door they found all the window glasses raised and the doors locked and the driver lying dead inside the car.	None
They tried to open the door of the car but were unable to open it.	None
Then they saw a car with a yellow light coming towards them from the opposite direction.	None
Seeing that car, both of them hid in the bushes, taking the cover of the wall behind them.	None
As soon as that car came near them, they fired at it at the same time shots were fired from the car, hitting Kasab on both his hands.	None
When the firing from the car stopped they looked at the car and found that the persons inside the car were policemen and all of them were dead.	None
They tried to open the cars rear door	None
but it did not open.	None
Kasab was injured and he stood leaning on the vehicle, shaking his hands, while Ismail fired a round of brush fire on the road behind the car.	None
Ismail then went near the car and pulled out the dead bodies of the driver and the policeman sitting behind the driver.	None
Kasab pulled out the dead body of the policeman sitting next to the driver and threw it on the ground.	None
There were no rounds left in Ismails Kalashan and, therefore, he picked up the policemans Kalashan from the car.	None
He started the car and drove at full speed.	None
He told Kasab that bullets had hit him on the legs and in the armpits.	None
After some time they reached the chowk and found a large crowd comprising both policemen and the public.	None
Ismail fired at the policemen and the public while continuing to drive the car.	None
After some time it appeared that the back right tyre of their car was punctured.	None
Ismail was, nevertheless, driving the car at a very high speed.	None
Then, on seeing a white car approaching from the opposite direction, Ismail stopped their car.	None
Kasab fired from his Kalashan in the air and both of them got out of the car.	None
He went towards the white car and, pointing the Kalashan at the driver, asked him to stop the car.	None
The driver immediately stopped the car.	None
Ismail pulled him out.	None
At the same time the person sitting next to the driver and the woman sitting on the back seat also got out.	None
All this while, Kasab was giving cover to Ismail.	None
Having thus snatched the car, Ismail sat on the drivers seat and Kasab quickly sat next to him and they left.	None
At this point Kasab asked Ismail where they had to go.	None
Ismail said they had to go to Malabar Hill.	None
Kasab further asked where exactly in Malabar Hill.	None
Ismail said he would tell him on reaching Malabar Hill.	None
After going for some distance, Kasab saw that they were traveling on a road going along the sea and then he realized that this road was shown in the map by Sabauddin and Fahim as going towards Malabar Hill.	None
While they were driving at full speed, going in the direction of Malabar Hill, they saw the barricade on the road and policemen standing around the barricade.	None
The policemen had seen their car moving at great speed from a long distance and were asking them to stop by raising their hands and blowing their whistles.	None
Realizing that it was impossible to cross the barricade by smashing against it, Kasab asked Ismail to stop the car at some distance from the barricade and to keep the headlights on so that the policemen would not be able to see either them or the number of their car.	None
Ismail stopped the car at some distance from the barricade and kept the headlights on.	None
The policemen were shouting at them and were asking them to switch off the headlights.	None
Looking around, Kasab saw that the road divider on his right was very low and thought they could cross it by driving the car at very high speed.	None
He advised Ismail accordingly.	None
Ismail immediately switched on the water spray on the wind screen and started the wiper.	None
He took the car a little ahead and turned it to the right in the direction of the road divider.	None
He drove at full speed but the car did not go over the divider and stopped there.	None
At the same time the policemen charged at them from both sides.	None
Realizing the gravity of the situation they both raised their hands.	None
But the policemen kept coming at them.	None
Seeing this Ismail tried to pick up the Kalashan	None
but it was kept below and he couldnt take it out.	None
He then picked up his pistol, which was kept on the seat, and fired at the policemen.	None
At the same time, Kasab saw a policeman coming towards him he opened the door of the car and got hold of his Kalashan.	None
The police had started firing.	None
A policeman tried to snatch the Kalashan from him.	None
In the struggle, Kasab fell down	None
but he had his finger on the trigger and he pressed it.	None
The bullets hit a policeman holding a rifle and he collapsed on the ground.	None
The other policemen beat him with lathis and snatched the Kalashan from his hands.	None
Ismail was injured in the police firing and he too was overpowered.	None
Kasab said that he and Ismail were then brought to the hospital in an ambulance.	None
In the hospital he learnt that Ismail died by police bullets.	None
He gave his and Ismails names to the police and the doctors and also told them that they were Pakistanis.	None
He concluded his statement before the magistrate by saying that the doctors in the hospital cleaned and bandaged his wounds and got him admitted in the hospital.	None
There the doctors took away his bloodsmeared clothes and gave him hospital clothes to wear.	None
When the police asked him about his colleagues and how they reached Bombay he told them everything.	None
This is the appellants account, as told by him to the magistrate.	None
We now propose to take a brief look at the violent crimes committed by the appellant and his group of terrorists in Mumbai through Indian eyes.	None
And for that we shall follow the bloody trails of the appellant and those of the other members of the terrorist group.	None
THE LANDING The inflatable rubber dinghy on which the terrorists came to Mumbai landed at a place called Badhwar Park.	None
The dinghys arrival at that particular place could not possibly be by accident or by chance.	None
Badhwar Park was evidently selected as the landing site for the terrorists with great care and with consideration of its immense strategic potential for the attack on their chosen targets.	None
It is also clear that the selection of Badhwar Park as their landing place was not made by the attackers themselves but by someone else among the conspirators.	None
The selection of the landing place for the dinghy was clearly based on a good deal of reconnaissance and survey work and whoever selected the spot for landing had undoubtedly made himself fully familiar not only with the Mumbai shore line but also the city.	None
Badhwar Park is a settlement of fishermen and at that place the sea comes more deeply into the land mass, forming a kind of a vesicle.	None
Hence, the water is calm and, this being a fishermens colony, a group of young people arriving from the sea is not likely to arouse any suspicion or even attract much attention.	None
Further, the place abutts a main road.	None
A sandy slope from the water, not more than ten (10) metres in length, takes one to the road where taxis are readily available.	None
The CST railway station is at distance of 3.5 kms from Badhwar Park and by a taxi it takes fifteen to twenty (1520) minutes to reach there.	None
The Taj Hotel is at distance of 1 km and Leopold Caf nine hundred (900) metres.	None
Nariman House, to which the two (2) terrorist went walking, is at a distance of 0.5 km.	None
Nariman Point, where the last pair took the dinghy by sea after the other eight had alighted at Badhwar Park, is 0.55 nautical miles (1 km) from there and from the point where the last pair got off the dinghy, Oberoi Hotel and Trident Hotel are at a distance of three hundred (300) metres.	None
The last pair walked to these hotels.	None
Kasab had said to the magistrate that on getting down from the boat they had come across two persons.	None
They had enquired about them and even while Abu Ismail tried to rebuff them Kasab told them that they were students.	None
One of these two men that Kasab met was Bharat Dattatray Tamore (PW28).	None
He lived in the Fisherman Colony, Cuffe Parade.	None
He was a permanent employee of Hotel Taj Mahal, Colaba, where he worked as Mukhadam.	None
He lived in Chawl no.2 which was situated very close to the sea shore at about fifteen (15) minutes walking distance from the Taj Hotel.	None
He deposed before the court that since his Chawl was very close to the shore, for going anywhere he had to go along the shore quite close to the water.	None
On November 26, 2008, he left his house at about 9.15 PM for the hotel, where his duties commenced at 10.00 PM and ended the following morning at 7.00 AM.	None
On the way to the hotel he saw an inflatable boat on the shore.	None
In the boat there were ten (10) people who were in the age group of twenty to twenty five (2025) years.	None
He saw eight out of them alighting from the boat.	None
Each of them was carrying a sack and a handbag.	None
Two of them proceeded towards the main road ahead of the others.	None
They appeared strangers to the place and he asked them where they came from.	None
One of them said they were students while the other responded by roughly asking in reply as to how he was concerned about them.	None
He added that the two persons who had not alighted took the boat towards Nariman Point.	None
He returned to his home next morning at about seven (700 AM).	None
On way he came across four (4) policemen near the Badhwar Park Railway Officers Colony who were talking about the inflatable boat.	None
He then told them what he had witnessed the previous evening.	None
He later identified the appellant in the test identification parade held on December 28, 2008.	None
He also identified the dead body of the other person at the mortuary of J.J. Hospital.	None
He also identified the appellant while deposing in court, as one of the persons who had alighted from the boat.	None
There is another person called Prashant Hemnath Dhanu (PW29) who lived in the fishermens colony.	None
He was twentyfour (24) years old and a fisherman by profession.	None
He stated before the court that he had a fishing boat and on November 26, 2008, at about 9.15 PM he, along with a few relatives, had gone out to sea on his boat to fish.	None
On nearing Nariman Point around 9.45 PM they saw a seemingly abandoned rubber boat.	None
There were some life jackets in the boat and it was fitted with a Yamaha engine.	None
Buffeted by the sea waves, it was bouncing against the tetrapod.	None
Lest the owner of the boat might suffer its loss they towed it to their fishing trawler and brought it to the jetty near the fishermens colony at Badhwar Park (that is, to the point where it had first landed).	None
He informed the coast guard about the abandoned boat found by him.	None
He further said that the police had arrived there and they took charge of the boat under a Panchnama.	None
We shall deal with the seizure of the boat by the police and the articles found in it in due course.	None
Suffice here to note that the rubber boat (Article 156) was shown to the witness in court and he duly identified it as the one that he had found abandoned at Nariman Point and had towed back to the Fishermens Colony, Badhwar Park.	None
He also indicated the yellow strip of paint on the black body of the boat, on the basis of which he was able to identify it.	None
From Badhwar Park the appellant, Kasab, and his accomplice, Abu Ismail, took a taxi and proceeded to CST.	None
Kasab told the magistrate that he occupied the back seat of the taxi and, on the way to CST, had put the RDX bomb under the drivers seat, setting the time of blast for after an hour and fifteen minutes.	None
We shall see the fate of the taxi, its driver and the passenger, who occupied it after Kasab and Abu Ismail, presently under the marginal heading The Vile Parle Blast.	None
But, for the present, the appellant and his buddy are on a spree of mass killings at CST.	None
Slaughter at CST Fifty two (52) dead and One hundred and nine (109) injured In regard to the CST episode, like all other parts of the case, the prosecution has gathered a very large amount of evidence ocular, forensic and of other kinds, e.g., CCTV recordings.	None
They have documented practically every action and movement of the two killers from the point when Abu Ismail threw the first hand grenade at the passengers on the platform till they went out of CST through the footoverbridge on the side of platform no.1 of the local lines (and thereafter.).	None
On the basis of the ocular evidence alone (not taking into account for the moment the other evidences)	None
the prosecution has presented before the court a vivid and photographic (figuratively and actually) account of the CST events.	None
Here we propose to examine in slightly greater detail four witnesses whose evidence, in one way or another, has some special features, and then to take an overview of some more witnesses to construct a broad picture of the massacre at CST.	None
Before proceeding to examine the witnesses it may be appropriate to say a word about the way most of the witnesses identified the appellant.	None
The appellant, Kasab, and his accomplice, Abu Ismail, seemed to make an odd pair in that Abu Ismail was quite tall, about six (6) feet in height, and Kasab is barely over five (5) feet.	None
The difference in their height appears to have struck almost anyone who saw them together.	None
Although different witnesses described them by their complexion (both Abu Ismail and Kasab are described as fair), age (Abu Ismail is said to be between 22 and 25 years and Kasab between 22 and 24 years), built of body (Abu Ismail as medium built, Kasab as strongly built), their apparel and the bags they were carrying, almost everyone referred to their heights, calling Abu Ismail as the taller and Kasab as the shorter one.	None
Many witnesses called them lamboo (tall) and butka or tingu (short).	None
Now the witnesses Bharat Ramchandra Bhosale (PW49) is the Informant in connection with the offences committed at CST.	None
At the time of the assault on CST he was an Assistant Inspector of Police attached to the CST Railway Police Station.	None
The police station is situated within the premises of CST in the passage between the main hall of local lines and the main hall of main lines.	None
On the night of November 26 and 27, he was on duty at the police station and he reported for duty at 20.30 hours.	None
At about 21.50 hours, while he was coming out of the PS, he heard the sound of firing from the main hall of the main line railway station.	None
The main hall is at a distance of about fifty to sixty (50 60) feet from the PS.	None
He proceeded to the main hall from the side of the taxi stand (north).	None
Police Inspector Shashank Shinde (one of the policemen killed in the attack), who was also on duty at that time, proceeded to the hall from the side of the SBI ATM (south).	None
On coming to the main hall he saw the two terrorists indiscriminately firing from AK47 rifles at the passengers sitting in the main hall.	None
Many people were lying injured in pools of blood many of them were crying.	None
Those who were still on their legs were trying to flee the main hall.	None
Bhosale said that he first saw the two terrorists when they were firing from a spot near the public toilet.	None
He described the location of the public toilet and went on to say that when he first saw the two terrorists they were in the main hall at a distance of about forty (40) feet.	None
There was sufficient light in the main hall for him to see them.	None
Bhosale then proceeded to give a description of the two terrorists.	None
He said that one of them was short, aged about twentytwo to twentyfour (2224) years with long hair that came down to his neck he had a fair complexion and was strongly built.	None
He was wearing a blue Tshirt and was carrying a rexine bag.	None
He was holding an AK47 rifle.	None
The other terrorist was taller than the first one.	None
He was also fair and of medium built.	None
He was aged about twentytwo to twentyfive (2225) years.	None
He was wearing a black Tshirt and he too was carrying a rexine bag.	None
He was also carrying an AK47 rifle.	None
At this point, the witness paused in his narration to identify the appellant as one of the two terrorists who was described by him as short, strong built and who was wearing a blue Tshirt.	None
The witness was then shown the identity card recovered from Abu Ismail (Article 61).	None
He identified the photograph as that of the other terrorist, the accomplice of the appellant.	None
The witness proceeded with his narration and said that he rushed back to the police station to ask for additional force.	None
As he came near the entrance door of the police station he was fired at by the terrorists.	None
One of the bullets pierced through his right upper arm and struck the wall near the table of the police stations House Officer.	None
He intimated the railway police helpline about the assault by the terrorists and asked for additional force.	None
He also intimated the Commissioner of Police, Railways, on his walkietalkie.	None
He then came back to the main hall accompanied by Police Constable Nalawade who had a carbine with him.	None
He saw Police Inspector Shinde lying injured near the SBI, ATM.	None
Also lying injured in the main hall were about one hundred to one hundred and twentyfive (100125) passengers.	None
By the time he came back to the main hall of the main lines, the two terrorists had moved in the direction of the main hall of the local railway station.	None
Constable Nalawade fired three rounds towards them from his carbine.	None
Constable Nardele (PW58) also fired eight rounds at them from the main hall of the main lines while the terrorists were in the main hall of the local lines.	None
The appellant and his associate were, however, not hit and they continued to proceed towards platform No. 1 of the local lines.	None
By then, the additional police force had come and the public had also come to their help.	None
The injured persons were being taken to hospitals.	None
The witness himself was admitted to St. Georges Hospital for treatment of the firearm injury in his right upper arm.	None
He later came to learn that Police Inspector Shinde and MN Chaudhary of the RPF were also among those who were killed as a result of the firing by the two terrorists.	None
He also learnt that the appellant and his associate had also used handgrenades at the railway station.	None
His statement was recorded at the hospital and on that basis a formal FIR was drawn up in regard to the CST episode.	None
He identified his statement (Ext. no. 219) and the formal FIR (Ext. no. 220).	None
He further told the court that he had earlier identified the appellant in the test identification parade held at Arthur Road Prison on December 28, 2008.	None
In reply to a court question, Bhosale said that though he was carrying a 9mm pistol, loaded with nine rounds, he did not fire at the terrorists because there was a strong risk of the passengers getting killed or injured by his firing.	None
Vishnu Dattaram Zende (PW65) is the railway announcer.	None
His job is to make announcements of the arrival and departure of trains on a public address system.	None
For that purpose he sits with his colleagues in a cabin on the mezzanine floor, almost at the centre of the main hall of the local lines, facing the full expanse of the main hall and beyond it up to platforms 1 to 7 of the local lines.	None
Perched in his office Zende had a completely unobstructed view through the glass screen of his cabin and he was able to see all that happening down below in the main hall and the local lines platforms on the fateful evening of November 26, 2008.	None
Here it must also be noted that showing great devotion to duty and remarkable presence of mind Zende saved countless people from death or injury by constantly announcing on the public address system that the railway station was under terrorist assault and by advising passengers alighting from local trains that continued to arrive at the station while the attack was underway to not go towards the main hall but to exit through the rear side of the local lines platforms.	None
Deposing before the court, he began with a succinct description of CST from inside.	None
He then proceeded to tell the court that on November 26, 2008, he was on duty from 3.00 PM to 11.00 PM.	None
At about 9.55 PM he heard a big explosion.	None
He guessed that it was a bomb and looked outside the window of his cabin.	None
He saw passengers from the main line hall running towards the local lines.	None
Among them some were bleeding.	None
Some were trying to rescue others who were unable to flee or move on account of injuries.	None
He further stated before the court that he saw two terrorists coming from the direction of platform no.7.	None
He could see one of them from a distance of 15 to 20 feet as he came near the entry gate of platform no. 4.	None
The other was following him.	None
Both were firing.	None
At that point he suspended his announcements because the terrorists, from where they were at that time, could see him and fire at him.	None
He then saw the shorter of the two terrorists sit down on the floor of the main hall, load his gun with a magazine, throw his bag in the hall and resume firing.	None
Zende added that, to avoid being shot at by the terrorists, he and his colleagues sat down on the floor of their cabin.	None
Nonetheless, shots were fired in the direction of their cabin and one of the bullets smashed the glass pane and went right through, piercing the plywood partition at the back of the cabin.	None
They continued sitting on the floor for about an hour and a half.	None
All the while they were in contact with their officers on the telephone.	None
He then gave a description of the two terrorists and identified Kasab as the person who loaded his rifle sitting down on the floor of the main hall and who threw away his bag.	None
He was then shown the identity card, Article 61.	None
He identified the photograph as that of the taller terrorist who was accompanying the appellant.	None
He was shown a black haversack, Article 219.	None

While dealing with the CST episode we must take note of two other witnesses.	None
Their evidence is extraordinary in that they did not only witness the incidents but also made a visual record of the events by taking pictures of the two killers in action and also of their victims.	None
The pictures taken by these two witnesses, without anything else, are sufficient to conclude the issue of identification of Kasab and Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) as the killers of CST.	None
Both the witnesses are professional photographers working with the Times of India group.	None
Both of them, caring little for their own safety and displaying exemplary professionalism, followed the killers practically at their heels.	None
Their ocular testimony together with the photographs taken by them provides a graphic picture of the carnage at CST.	None

Among the rest of the CST witnesses we shall take a brief look first at some of the policemen and then at some of the passenger witnesses.	None
Jilu Baddu Yadav (PW54), Mammath Motiral Nardele (PW58), Harshad Punju Patil (PW59), Geetanjali Krishnarao Gurav (PW60), Sudama Aba Pandarkar (PW62), Pandurang Subrao Patil (PW63) and Sandeep Tanaji Khiratkar (PW66) are policemen or members of the Railway Protection Force.	None
At the time of occurrence, they were on duty at different places in the vast premises of CST.	None
On hearing the explosion and the gun shots and on seeing the passengers fleeing for their lives, they realized that a terrorist attack was underway at the railway station and proceeded from their respective stations towards the spot where the assault was launched.	None
On the way, some of them came across each other.	None
A few were lucky to escape unharmed and some survived even after receiving grave injuries to tell the story before the court some others laid down their lives while trying to tackle the assailants either completely unarmed or carrying antiquated weapons that failed them at the most crucial moment.	None
Harshad Punju Patil (PW59) was a police constable and on that date he was on patrolling duty in the ladies compartment in the local trains.	None
He was carrying a .303 rifle and ten (10) rounds.	None
When the terrorists attack took place, he was waiting for the train on which he was on duty near the Police Help Center in the main hall of the local lines, in front of platform no.3.	None
Soon after the firing started, Police Inspector Shashank Shinde of the CST Railway Police Station came there and told them that two terrorists were firing in the main hall of the main station.	None
Police constables Nardele and Gavit were also there.	None
Both of them were carrying carbines.	None
Shashank Shinde proceeded towards the main line station accompanied by Nardele and Gavit.	None
Patil started loading the ten (10) rounds in his rifle.	None
He then saw the two terrorists coming towards the local railway station from the main lines side.	None
Taking cover of the Police Help Centre he fired one round at them.	None
But the shot misfired because the cartridge was defective the bolt was jammed and he was unable to open it.	None
By that time, the terrorists had come in front of platform no.3 of the local lines.	None
At that point, Jillu Baddu Yadav (PW54), a head constable of the RPF, also arrived there, proceeding from his place of duty at the General Manager Gate of the CST Railway Station.	None
He himself was unarmed but he saw Patil carrying a rifle with him.	None
He saw one of the assailants sitting down on the floor of the main hall of the local station and loading his rifle with a magazine.	None
Yadav asked Patil to fire at the terrorist.	None
He did not know that Patils rifle bolt had jammed and it would not open.	None
Thinking that Patil was trying to avoid firing at the terrorist, Yadav took the rifle from him and tried to fire at the terrorist who was sitting down on the station floor, loading the magazine into the rifle, but the rifle did not fire as it had locked.	None
Meanwhile, the other terrorist also arrived at the spot and they fired in the direction of Yadav and Patil.	None
He and Patil then took cover behind a pillar from where he threw one plastic chair towards the two terrorists.	None
In retaliation they again fired back towards them while proceeding in the direction of platform no.1 of the local railway station.	None
Patil identified the appellant as the one whom he had described as the shorter of the two terrorists.	None
He identified Abu Ismail (deceased accused no. 1) from his photograph on the fake identity card, Article 61.	None
He said before the court that he had earlier identified the appellant in the test identification parade held on January 14, 2009, at Arthur Road Prison.	None
Yadav identified the appellant as the person who was firing at him from his AK47 rifle and at whom he had thrown the plastic chair.	None
Yadav also identified Abu Ismail from Article 61.	None
Mammath Motiral Nardele (PW58) was a police constable and on that date he was on antisabotage duty on the footoverbridge at platform no.1, opposite the Times of India building.	None
He was carrying a carbine with ten (10) rounds.	None
At about 9.45 PM, leaving his two other colleagues on duty, he came to take his meal at the Police Help Centre situated in front of platform no.3 of the local railway station.	None
No sooner had he reached there that he heard the noise of a bomb explosion and gun shots from the direction of the main hall of the main lines and saw passengers running away from there.	None
Shashank Shinde came there and alerted him saying that terrorists were firing in the main hall of the main line.	None
Shinde asked Nardele to accompany him.	None
Nardele started loading the ten (10) rounds in his carbine but Shinde proceeded towards the main line without waiting for him.	None
Nardele saw Shinde proceeding in the direction of the main hall of the main line accompanied by ASI Pandarkar PW62, Injured shown in photograph Ext. no.	None
245, a police constable Ambadas Pawar, killed shown lying down with Shashank Shinde in photograph Ext.	None
no. 242 and a photographer PW61, Dsouza.	None
He went after them and heard the sound of firing on platform no.7.	None
He entered a compartment of a local train on platform no.6 and from there he saw two terrorists, each carrying an AK47 rifle and a handbag on their shoulders, proceeding towards the local railway station.	None
He fired eight (8) rounds from his carbine (but the shots did not hit them).	None
They retaliated but he was safe inside the rail compartment.	None
He again tried to fire, but in the meanwhile his carbine was locked.	None
He could not fire from it any longer.	None
He then went to the armory, got his carbine unlocked and loaded it with more rounds.	None
But by the time he came back to the main hall of the local lines, the terrorists had already left the local railway station.	None
Nardele identified the appellant in court as the shorter of the two terrorists.	None
He also identified the clothes worn by the two assailants.	None
He also identified Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) from Article 61.	None
He further told the court that he had earlier identified the appellant in the test identification parade held on December 28, 2008, at Arthur Road Prison, Mumbai.	None
He had also identified the dead body of the deceased accused no.1 at the mortuary of JJ Hospital on January 6, 2009.	None
Sudama Aba Pandarkar (PW62) was an Assistant SubInspector of police and on November 26, 2008, he was on patrolling duty on the local trains.	None
He was carrying a .303 rifle and ten (10) rounds.	None
The train on which he was on duty arrived at CST on platforms no. 4 or 5 at 9.45 PM.	None
He went to the Police Help Center and made the entry concerning his patrolling duty.	None
Within a few minutes the explosion took place followed by firing, and he saw many passengers running wildly.	None
In the meantime, Shashank Shinde came to the Police Help Center.	None
He told them that the railway station was under attack by terrorists.	None
Shinde asked Pandarkar to load his 303 rifle.	None
Pandarkar accompanied Shinde towards the main line.	None
He saw a terrorist who was about 6 feet in height coming from the side of the taxi stand and firing towards the railway police station.	None
At that time he was standing in front of the railway police station.	None
He fired two rounds at him from his .303 rifle but the shots did not hit him.	None
At this point, Police Constable Ambadas Pawar, who was also accompanying Shinde, took the rifle from Pandarkar and fired one round at the terrorist.	None
At the same time Pandarkar saw the other terrorist (the appellant) coming towards them from the side of platform no.8 (main line).	None
He was shorter in height than the other terrorist.	None
He was firing from his AK47 rifle.	None
Pandarkar, Constable Ambadas Pawar and PI Shinde went towards platform no.7 through platform no.6 and came near the ATM of Indian Bank.	None
Both the terrorists started firing at them from AK47 rifles.	None
One of the bullets pierced through Pandarkars left chest and exited from the back.	None
He fell down as a result of the bullet injury.	None
Shashank Shinde and Ambadas Pawar too were hit by the terrorists shots	None
and unfortunately they were not as lucky as Pandarkar.	None
They succumbed to their injuries.	None

Sandeep Tanaji Khiratkar (PW66) was an Inspector in the Railway Protection Force.	None
At the time of the occurrence he was at his residence and was informed about the attack by Jadhav (PW54) by telephone.	None
He rushed to the police station on his motorcycle and arrived there in five to seven (57) minutes.	None
He went to the RPF armory on the ground floor of the General Manager Office building and took out a .303 rifle and twenty (20) rounds from the armory.	None
He came out of the station from the GM Porch abutting DN Road.	None
SI Bhosale (PW68) and Inspector Kshirsagar were with him.	None
They took position in the GM Porch.	None
At that time they saw two terrorists coming towards the porch situated near the subway.	None
Both the terrorists fired at them.	None
They also retaliated and fired back at the terrorists.	None
The firing by Khiratkar and his men forced the terrorists to reenter the railway station and move in the opposite direction towards platform no. 1 from where they went out of the railway station through the footoverbridge.	None
When Khiratkar and his men reached near the gate of the footoverbridge they were informed that the terrorists had already left the railway station.	None
Khiratkar then went to the control room of the CCTV cameras in the RPF office.	None
There he found that on that date the CCTV cameras of the main lines were shut down for maintenance but the movements of Kasab and Abu Ismail were recorded by the CCTV cameras in the main hall and platform no.1 of the local lines.	None
At about 11.30 PM on the same day, he was informed by Constable Jadhav that the movements of the terrorists had been recorded on the Data Visual Recorder.	None
Immediately thereafter he prepared from the DVR a CD of the visuals captured by CCTV cameras of the main hall and other places wherever the movements of the terrorists had been seen.	None
The CD was sealed by him immediately and it was later handed over to an officer of DCB CID, Mumbai.	None
He further stated before the court that the recording on the DVR is stored for a period of seven days.	None
At the end of the seventh day the first days recording would get deleted to make space for the recording of the eighth day.	None
Khiratkar identified the appellant as the shorter of the two terrorists.	None
He identified Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) from his photograph on Article 61.	None
He had earlier identified the appellant in the test identification parade held on December 28, 2008, at Arthur Road prison, Mumbai.	None
Pandurang Subrao Patil (PW63) was an Assistant SubInspector of Police on duty carrying a lathi.	None
He told the court that he was fired at by the shorter terrorist (i.e., the appellant).	None
The bullet hit his left thigh and, passing through it, pierced his right thigh and exited from the exterior portion of his right thigh.	None
He simply collapsed on to the floor.	None
He further said that he had seen the two terrorists from a distance of twentytwo to twentyfive (22 to 25) feet.	None

Geetanjali Krishnarao Gurav (PW60) was on duty at the CST local railway station near main gate no. 3.	None
On hearing the explosion and the gun shots she along with Shinde (killed), API Bhosale (PW49), PSI Khandale and other policemen went towards the main hall of the main lines.	None
She saw two terrorists in the main hall and she saw the taller of the two throwing a hand grenade at a crowd of passengers.	None
The grenade exploded, causing injuries to a large number of passengers.	None
Both terrorists were continuously firing from AK47 rifles.	None
She and Bhosale, therefore, proceeded towards the railway police station to call for additional force.	None
While on way to the police station, Bhosale was hit by a bullet in his left upper arm and he fell down.	None
She tied a handkerchief to his wound and helped him in getting back on his feet.	None
At that time, she saw both the terrorists proceeding in the direction of the local railway station.	None
More than hundred (100) passengers lay badly injured in the main hall of the main lines.	None
Geetanjali Gurav identified the appellant as the shorter of the two terrorists.	None
She also identified Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) from his photograph on Article 61.	None
Now, some of the passengers Natwarlal Gigaji Rotawan (PW50) and his daughter Devika Natwarlal Rotawan, aged about ten (10) years, (PW51) Farooqi Nasiruddin Khaliluddin (PW52) Nafisa Shadab Qureshi (PW53) Sangeeta Niranjan Sardar (PW86) and her husband Niranjan Sadashiv Sardar (PW87) and Ansar Alabaksha Mohd.	None
Hanif Saudagar (PW88), are some of the passenger witnesses.	None
They were in the main hall of the main lines waiting for their respective trains.	None
They were jolted out of whatever they might be doing or thinking at that moment by the explosion of the first grenade thrown by Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1) and from that moment they watched, in abject horror, the appellant and his companion firing indiscriminately at the group of passengers in the main hall Abu Ismail throwing the second grenade and then the two moving around on the platforms in different directions until the spray of bullets and the shrapnel from the exploding grenades hit them or one of their group.	None
Natwarlal Rotawan (PW50) was lucky to escape unhurt but his daughter, Devika Rotawan (PW51), was hit by a bullet on her right leg.	None
She was treated as an indoor patient in the hospital for about a month and a half and thereafter remained bedridden for four to six (46) months.	None
When she came to depose in court after about 6 months of the occurrence, she was still unable to walk properly.	None
Natwarlal identified the appellant as the shorter one and said that his companion was not present in court.	None
Devika identified the appellant as the person who was firing at the VT railway station.	None
Farooqi Nasiruddin Khaliluddin (PW52) was at the station with his son.	None
Both of them were injured, the son far more badly than the father, by the splinters from the second grenade thrown by Abu Ismail (deceased accused no. 1).	None
Khaliluddin told the court that the firing by the terrorists continued for about fifteen to twenty (1520) minutes.	None
He further said that the taller man had paused in the firing as he took out a bomb from his bag and threw it in their direction but that the other man (that is, the appellant) continued with the firing and he appeared to be in a joyous mood on seeing the lethal effect of his firing.	None
Identifying the appellant in court, he once again said that he was the same person whom he had seen in joyous mood.	None
Nafisa Qureshi (PW53), who worked as a maidservant, lost her six (6) year old daughter Afrin to the terrorists bullets.	None
She was hit by a bullet on the back and died at the spot.	None
Nafisa herself sustained a bullet injury on her left leg.	None
She identified the appellant as one of the two persons who were firing at CST in all directions.	None
The appellant was the person whom she had, earlier in her deposition, referred to as the shorter one.	None

Sangeeta was hit by steel balls (from the hand grenade) that pierced her body, and some of which were still lodged inside her body as she deposed.	None
Her husband, Niranjan, sustained two (2) bullet injuries, one on the right side of the head and the other below the right ear.	None
Both of them remained indoor patients in the hospital for weeks.	None
