Cama In Seven (7) dead and ten (10) injured Kasab and Abu Ismail were seen exiting CST via the footoverbridge and coming down the bridge in the evidence of Vernekar (PW102) and in the photograph of Kasab (Ext. no. 410D) taken by him.	None
On descending from the footoverbridge, they came to Badruddin Tayabji Marg, which is a long, meandering road, a part of which runs along the premises of Cama Hospital.	None
Cama Hospital has large premises, on which there are a number of buildings including a sixstorey structure called the New Hospital Building.	None
The entry to Cama Hospital is from Mahapalika Road on its western side, and Badruddin Tayabji Marg runs along the back of its premises.	None
The prosecution, with the aid of eleven (11) eyewitnesses, has traced practically every step taken by Kasab and Abu Ismail from the moment they came out of CST, entered Cama hospital and eventually left the hospital.	None
We, however, propose to examine only some of these steps, to get a broad idea of how the two were moving around killing people, completely mindlessly.	None
Bharat Budhabhai Waghela (PW103) worked as a Safai Kamgar with Voltas.	None
He lived in a hut off Badruddin Tayabji Marg.	None
At about 9.30 PM on November 26, 2008, he was sitting near the back gate of Cama Hospital on Badruddin Tayabji Marg engaged in small talk with his friends Sandeep Waghela (PW105), who lived on the premises of Cama Hospital, and Bhagan Shinde, who lived in the same hutments as Waghela.	None
Gupta bhelvendor was also near the gate selling snacks of bhelpuri.	None
At about 10.30 PM they saw two persons coming on to Badruddin Tayabji Road from the direction of the Times of India Building.	None
One of them was lamboo (tall) and the other was butka (short).	None
Both were carrying bags on their shoulders.	None
Suddenly, they started firing.	None
The butka man fired straight at them, and he shot Gupta bhelwala in full view of Waghela.	None
Waghela was frightened and ran towards his hut.	None
His friends also ran away from the spot.	None
Back in his hut, Waghela told his mother about the incident.	None
He shut the doors of his hut and peeped out from the little gap between the frame of the door and the panels.	None
He saw the butka fellow standing near his brothers shanty, adjoining Waghelas own hut, and firing at it.	None
He heard his brother cry out.	None
He saw the lamboo fellow firing in the lane.	None
After some time, he saw both of them going towards the gate of Cama Hospital.	None
After a while, Waghela went to his brother, Thakur Waghelas shanty.	None
He found his brother lying in a pool of blood.	None
His five (5) year old son was also there but his wife was not present.	None
Waghela took his brother to the GT Hospital where he was declared dead by the doctors.	None
Five minutes later, Bhagan Shinde was brought to the hospital.	None
He was also declared dead.	None
Waghela identified the appellant as the gunman who had shot Gupta bhelwala and fired at his brothers shanty.	None
He said before the court that he had identified the accused in the test identification parade on December 27, 2008.	None
He had also identified the dead body of the lamboo when it was placed among six (6) other dead bodies at the mortuary of JJ Hospital.	None
He then identified him from the photograph on the identity card, Article 61.	None
Anjali Vijay Kulathe (PW101) worked as a staff nurse at Cama Hospital.	None
On November 26, 2008, she arrived for duty at 8.00 PM.	None
She was on duty on the first floor of the New Building.	None
At about 10.30 PM she heard the sound of firing from the back of the hospital.	None
She looked out from the back window of the antenatal care unit and saw two persons climbing over the steel gate at the back of the hospital.	None
One of them was lamboo (tall) and the other was butka (short).	None
She could see them clearly in the light from the street lights.	None
She further said that the gate was at the distance of ten to fifteen (1015) feet from the window from where she saw the intruders.	None
The two men jumped inside the Cama Hospital premises.	None
The tall man fired towards the window from where she was looking at them.	None
One of the bullets hit the right wrist of a hospital servant, Hira Jadhav.	None
She was immediately removed to the casualty ward on the ground floor of the hospital.	None
Kulathe further said that she informed the CMO on duty, Dr. Archana, that two terrorists had entered the hospital building.	None
She then rushed back to her ward and closed all the doors from inside.	None
She also locked the wards collapsible (iron grill) gate.	None
Moreover, since the ward had windows on all sides, all twenty (20) patients who were in the ANC ward at that time were moved to the pantry for their safety.	None
She further stated before the court that the noise of firing and explosions went on for about two hours.	None
She and all the patients were frightened due to the continuous noise of explosions and firing.	None
She and the patients stayed inside the pantry till 4.00 AM the following morning, when senior officers came and took them out.	None
She then identified the appellant as the butka man who, along with his tall partner, had entered the Cama Hospital premises by jumping over its back gate.	None
She identified the tall partner of the appellant from the photograph on the identity card, Article 61.	None
She further told the court that she had identified the appellant in the test identification parade on December 27, 2008, held by judge (sic) Sharad Vichare.	None
She further said that, on being identified by her, the appellant had said that he was in fact Ajmal Kasab and she had correctly identified him.	None
Raosaheb Changdev Funde (PW107) is an exserviceman and he worked as an unarmed security guard at Cama Hospital.	None
On November 26, 2008, his shift ended at 10.00 PM but he learnt that some incidents had taken place at CST and, therefore, decided not to go home but to stay back for the night at the hospital.	None
He stated before the court that, on learning about the CST incidents, he returned to Cama Hospitals main (front) gate, near the collapsible gate.	None
Another security guard, Baban Ugade, was also there.	None
As Funde was standing with Ugade near the collapsible gate, he saw the appellant and one other person coming towards them.	None
The appellant fired a shot at Ugade from his rifle.	None
The shot hit Ugade in the abdomen and he fell down.	None
Funde was scared and ran up the stairs to the fifth floor, where he took shelter in a ward, hiding behind a stand which is used for drying clothes.	None
The appellant, however, followed him there and, putting the barrel of his rifle on his head, ordered him, Utho (getup).	None
The appellant then asked Funde to proceed towards the bathroom.	None
Funde saw one person lying in a pool of blood in front of the bathroom with a tall man standing near him.	None
The appellant made him enter the bathroom where three (3) persons were already confined The bathroom was then bolted from outside.	None
After two to three (2 or 3) hours, the police arrived there and opened the bathroom.	None
Funde narrated the incident to the police.	None
Funde then identified the appellants partner from the photograph on the identity card, Article 61.	None
He further told the court the he had identified the appellant at the test identification parade on December 27, 2008.	None
He had also identified the dead body of the appellants partner on January 7, 2009, at JJ Hospital.	None
Harishchandra Sonu Shrivardhankar (PW106) was the person whom Funde had seen lying in a pool of blood near the door of the bathroom.	None
His encounter with the two terrorists has something uncanny about it.	None
Fate seemed to force his every step towards meeting the terrorists and when he actually stood facetoface with them, quite certain of death, he did not go down without fighting.	None
Tough, two and a half times the age of his opponents, completely unarmed and untrained in any kind of fighting, he put up a fight nonetheless.	None
Unfortunately, his attempt could not succeed against an armed and trained killer.	None
He was stabbed and shot and left behind by the terrorist in the belief that he was dead or would soon die.	None
Shrivardhankar, however, survived to tell the story and to identify his assailant.	None
Shrivardhankar worked as a Senior Clerk at the Mantralaya at the time.	None
Apparently a devotee of Hazrat Sayyed Shah Baba (a Muslim saint), after leaving his office at 6.00 PM on November 26, 2008, Shrivardhankar went to the Urs at the saints Durgah (shrine), situated behind Metro Cinema.	None
He left the Durgah at 10.30 PM and proceeded to CST via the Metro subway and St. Xaviers College to catch a train home.	None
On approaching the gate of Cama Hospital at Mahapalika Road, Shrivardhankar saw many people running in panic and learnt about the incident of firings at CST.	None
To avoid getting caught in the firing, he sought refuge in Cama Hospital.	None
On entering the gate of the hospital he saw a dead body (Ugade) lying in front of the entrance to the main building.	None
On seeing the dead body he was scared and, suspecting that some incident must have taken place on the premises of the hospital, he entered the main building through the collapsible gate.	None
There was complete silence in the building and he found all the doors closed.	None
He went up to the fourth floor all the floors appeared to be deserted and the doors of all the wards were closed.	None
As soon as he reached the fifth floor, the luckless man found himself standing in front of a man holding a gun and a knife, and carrying a bag on his shoulder.	None
He was about five feet six inches (5 6) tall and had short hair.	None
He was wearing a jacket.	None
He put his knife on Shrivardhankars neck.	None
Shrivardhankar realised that the man would kill him in any case and, therefore, decided to fight.	None
He tried to hit the man in the groin with his knee and also attempted to hit him with his bag.	None
The bag, however, slipped out of Shrivardhankars hand and the killer struck him two (2) times on the neck with his knife, causing bleeding.	None
The killer caught hold of Shrivardhankars collar and pushed him down.	None
He inflicted a third knife blow on his back and also shot a bullet in his back.	None
By that time, Shrivardhankar had lost any strength to resist and fell unconscious.	None
He regained consciousness after three to four (34) days at JJ Hospital and was treated as an indoor patient for about three (3) months.	None
Shrivardhankar vividly recounted his encounter with one of the terrorists.	None
He also told the court that in the fight with the killer his spectacles had fallen down.	None
At that time he was wearing brown slippers (footwear).	None
Shrivardhankar told the court that his footwear and spectacles were lost and he did not find them on regaining consciousness at JJ Hospital.	None
He then identified his assailant at Cama Hospital from the photograph on the identity card, Article 61.	None
He also identified the assailant in the photographs Ext. no.	None

Chandrakant Dnyandev Tikhe (PW109) was the lift operator at Cama Hospital.	None
On November 26, 2008, he was on duty as Generator Operator from 10.00 PM in the evening till 700 AM the following morning.	None
The generator room is situated on the terrace of the building.	None
At about 1000 PM, when he was on the terrace, Tikhe heard the sound of firing from the ground floor.	None
On hearing the gunshots he immediately went inside the enclosure where the solar system is installed and locked its collapsible gate.	None
He was still inside the enclosure when, around 1100 PM, the two terrorists arrived on the terrace.	None
He saw them clearly in the light of the electric bulb of 200 watts that was lit on the terrace.	None
One of them was taller and the other was shorter.	None
The butka (short) fellow pointed his rifle towards Tikhe and asked him to come out or else he would blow him to bits (Aage aao warna uda dunga).	None
Therefore, Tikhe opened the gate and came out of the enclosure.	None
The tall man was also holding a gun.	None
Tikhe then identified the appellant as the short man who had pointed his gun at him.	None
When Tikhe came out of the enclosure, the appellant asked him the way out from the hospital.	None
Tikhe told them that there was only one staircase that alone could be used to exit the hospital.	None
The tall fellow, who was keeping a watch, suddenly shouted Police and started firing towards the stairs.	None
The appellant held his gun against Tikhes back and pushed him towards the stairs.	None
The appellant and his tall partner brought Tikhe to the landing between the sixth floor and the terrace.	None
From there, Tikhe saw three to four (34) policemen in front of the lift on the sixth floor.	None
Tikhe raised his hands apprehending that he might be killed by the police if they suspected him of being a terrorist.	None
A staff member of Cama Hospital, namely Kailash (PW111), was also with the policemen and he identified Tikhe to the police as one of the hospital staff.	None
The police fired at the appellant and his tall partner forcing them to retreat to the terrace.	None
In that time, Tikhe escaped and came down to the sixth floor landing.	None
He told the police that there were two terrorists.	None
The appellant then started firing at them from above.	None
He also threw a hand grenade on to the sixth floor.	None
The splinters from the hand grenade hit Tikhe on his neck and he sustained a bleeding injury.	None
Some policemen were also injured from the explosion of the hand grenade.	None
The appellant and his tall partner kept firing at the policemen.	None
Tikhe saw a police officer and another policeman getting shot and falling down in front of the lift.	None
After some time, the terrorists again threw down a hand grenade and fired indiscriminately in the direction of the lift.	None
The other policemen and the officers were also injured by the second explosion and the firing.	None
At this point, Tikhe came down to the second floor.	None
He was accompanied by two policemen and by Kailash.	None
One of these policemen went further down but the other stayed with them.	None
After being given first aid they were shifted to GT Hospital.	None
From there, Tikhe was taken to KEM Hospital for treatment as hand grenade splinters were lodged in his neck.	None
He was treated as an indoor patient for seven (7) days.	None
He also told the court that he had identified the appellant in the test identification parade on December 27, 2008.	None
Sadanand Vasant Date (PW118) is an IPS Officer and, at the material time, he was posted as Additional Commissioner of Police, Central Region, Mumbai.	None
On November 26, 2008, at about 10.00 PM, he was at his residence when the assault at CST took place.	None
CST did not come within his jurisdiction but, on the request of his colleague Dr. Vankatesham whose jurisdiction included CST, Date came out like any dutiful police officer.	None
He first went to the Malabar Hill Police Station, which was close to his residence, and collected one carbine and twenty (20) rounds.	None
On the way to CST he got information about the movements of the terrorists and, in light of this information, he and his team reached Cama Hospital a little after 11.00 PM.	None
Date came to learn that the terrorists had gone up to the terrace of Cama Hospital building and, therefore, he took the lift to the sixth floor landing, from where stairs led up to the terrace holding Tikhe there.	None
On reaching the sixth floor, instead of rushing to the terrace, Date picked up an iron object lying there and threw it towards the door of the terrace, to check the position of the terrorists.	None
In response, a burst of firing from an automatic weapon came from the terrace door.	None
Shortly thereafter, Date saw a bulky person (Tikhe) coming down to the landing on the stairs between the terrace and the 6th floor.	None
Date challenged the bulky person but Kailash (PW111) identified him as a member of the hospital staff.	None
The bulky person indicated that there was somebody behind him.	None
Date asked him to bend down and then fired over his head towards the terrace.	None
That forced the terrorists to go back to the terrace.	None
Taking advantage of the situation, Tikhe came down to the sixth floor landing.	None
In the meantime, a grenade was thrown from the terrace.	None
It exploded on the sixth floor in front of the lift causing injuries to some police officers, including Date, and also to Tikhe.	None
Dates team comprised seven (7) police officers and policemen.	None
All of them were armed with firearms.	None
Dates operator Tilekar and police constable Khandelkar had one carbine each.	None
Date himself was wearing a bulletproof jacket and he had a carbine with twenty (20) rounds.	None
But all this did not prove sufficient to take out Kasab and Abu Ismail or even to stop them.	None
The two terrorists were able to overcome the police and to escape from the tight spot in which they had landed the terrace that had only one (1) exit by the stairs.	None
This was because, besides having superior fire power, they had the great advantage of hand grenades.	None
Grenades exploding in the very small landing area badly injured the policemen who had no cover or shelter there.	None
Date stated before the court that, after the first hand grenade exploded, his officers continued to fire towards the terrace.	None
But shortly afterwards, another hand grenade was thrown, which caused injuries to almost all officers who were present there, including Date.	None
The injured police officers, policemen and staff members of Cama Hospital were asked to go down.	None
More (killed) could not go down because he was badly injured and unconscious.	None
Police constable Khandekar (killed) also could not go down as he, too, was badly injured.	None
Date said before the court that he continued to fire towards the terrace in retaliation of the firing from there.	None
The exchange of fire went on for about forty (40) minutes during which he had taken cover behind a wall situated in front of the right side lift.	None
After some time he sensed some movement and, as he came out from behind the wall which he was using for cover, he found that two persons had already gone down towards the fifth floor.	None
He fired two shots towards the two persons going away but was unable to say whether or not they were hit.	None
He was unable to pursue them because of his leg injury.	None
He said it would be 11.50 PM at that time.	None
Accordingly, Date informed his superiors that two persons had gone down from the sixth floor of the building and that they had automatic weapons and hand grenades.	None
Date further said that the help came at about 00.45 AM and he was shifted to KEM Hospital, where he was admitted for three (3) days.	None
Apart from several minor injuries he had sustained injuries from splinters and fragments of the hand grenade in his right eye and on the left side of chest just below armpit, and in his throat, right knee and left ankle.	None
Cama Out Nine (9) dead, seven (7) injured Date on the sixth floor landing was unable to stop Kasab and Abu Ismail and, while he took shelter against the hail of bullets and shrapnel from the grenades behind a wall, the two managed to sneak down the stairs.	None
Suresh Shantaram Kadam (PW138) and Yashwant Shankar Thorawade (PW128) next saw Kasab and Abu Ismail coming out of Cama Hospital from its front side on Mahapalika Road and immediately gunning down a police officer.	None
Thorawade was a Police Inspector and, on the evening of November 26, 2008, in the absence of the senior police inspector, he was holding charge of Azad Maidan police station.	None
Kadam was a constable attached to the same Police Station.	None
As Azad Maidan police station received information that terrorists had entered CST and were firing there, the policemen proceeded to the railway station in two police vehicles.	None
On the way, they learnt that the terrorists had left the railway station and were seen going in the direction of Metro Cinema.	None
Accordingly, they came to Metro junction where they came across Additional Police Commissioner Date (PW118).	None
Date asked them to go back and collect bulletproof jackets and arms and ammunition from Azad Maidan police station as information had arrived by then that the terrorists had reached the terrace of Cama Hospital building and were firing from there.	None
As directed by Date, Kadam, Shelke (PW141) and some others went back to Azad Maidan police station where they collected two bulletproof jackets and some firearms and ammunition.	None
Returning to the scene of firing, they decided to go to the front gate of Cama Hospital (instead of going to the back side), expecting the terrorists to exit the hospital from its main gate.	None
Kadam stated that he was accompanied by PI Thorawade (PW128), PSI Shelke (PW141), and police constables Utekar and Rathore.	None
Constable Gawade was driving the Bolero vehicle (called PeterI	None
Azad Maidan) in which they came there.	None
The vehicle was parked on the left side of the road facing Metro junction and they took position by the side of the vehicle.	None
At about 1145 PM, the policemen saw two persons coming out of Cama Hospital.	None
Kadam first saw them on the footpath of Cama Hospital and Thorawade when they were near the gate of St. Xaviers College adjoining the hospital.	None
Kadam said that one of them was lamboo (tall) and the other was butka (short).	None
In the meantime, they saw a motorcycle driving on Mahapalika Road from Metro junction towards CST.	None
It was driven by a police constable and a police officer was on its pillion.	None
The officer got down near the gate of St. Xaviers College and, according to Kadam, the motorcycle went ahead.	None
(According to Thorwade, the constable made a uturn and went back towards Metro).	None
The officer who got down from the motorcycle started directing people coming from the direction of CST to return.	None
He seemed to have asked the lamboo and the butka also not to proceed further but to go back.	None
But they continued moving towards him and fired at him from a distance of about fifteen to twenty (1520) feet.	None
The officer collapsed to the ground.	None
This confirmed to Thorawade and Kadam that the two persons who had come out from Cama Hospital were the terrorists whom they had been watching for.	None
Thorawade started firing at them from his service pistol.	None
Kadam also fired one round from his pistol and then he stopped because Thorawade was firing at the terrorists.	None
The terrorists fired back in retaliation.	None
Thorawade told the court that he tried sending messages to South Control from the wireless installed in his Bolero police vehicle but, due to heavy traffic on the network, he was unable to send the message.	None
Therefore, Thorawade went to the Metro junction where two to three (23) police vehicles were available.	None
The message was sent from the wireless set of one of those vehicles.	None
There were many people at the metro junction.	None
After a short while, one police vehicle (Qualis) appeared from Badruddin Tayabji Road and took right turn on Mahapalika Road towards Metro junction.	None
Thorawade saw the two terrorists in that vehicle.	None
The person who was sitting on the right side was firing at the large crowd assembled at Metro junction.	None
One policeman and another person were injured due to firing from that vehicle.	None
In the meanwhile, Kadam had remained in front of Cama Hospital.	None
He went on to state before the court that he saw a white car with a red beacon approaching Mahapalika Road from Badruddin Tayabji Road but, immediately thereafter, he saw the car going backwards on Badruddin Tayabji Road.	None
The lamboo and the butka fired at that car.	None
One of them also threw a handgrenade towards the white car.	None
Thereafter, both of them proceeded towards Rang Bhavan Lane on (BT Road).	None
The officer who was shot near the gate of St. Xaviers College was later identified from the name plate on his uniform as Durgude.	None
Kadam then identified Kasab in the dock as the butka who had fired at Durgude and who was accompanying the lamboo.	None
Kadam further stated that he had earlier identified the appellant in the identification parade on December 27, 2008, and had also identified the dead body of the lamboo on January 6, 2009, at the JJ Hospital mortuary.	None
Maruti Madhavrao Phad (PW139) was the driver of the white car with red beacon which Kadam had seen coming from Badruddin Tayabji Road towards Mahapalika Road and then going in the reverse direction.	None
It was actually a white Honda City car, a government vehicle allotted to one Bhushan Gagrani, IAS, Secretary Medical Education and Drugs Department (PW140).	None
Phad was the driver on duty for the vehicle.	None
On November 26, 2008, at 6.30 PM the car was, as usual, parked in the premises of High Rise Building situated on Badruddin Tayabji Road.	None
Between 1130 and 1145 PM, Phad received a call on his mobile from Gagrani, asking him to bring the car to his residence to take him to Mantralaya to attend an emergency meeting that seems to have been called as news broke of the terrorists attack on Mumbai.	None
As directed, Phad took the car from its parking place on Badruddin Tayabji Road and proceeded towards Mahapalika Road on his way to Gagranis residence.	None
As he approached Mahapalika Road, Phad saw two persons, one tall and the other short, firing on the road.	None
He, therefore, stopped the car and began to reverse.	None
At this, those two persons fired at his vehicle.	None
Phads right hand was on the steering wheel.	None
Two bullets pierced the cars windscreen and hit him on his right hand.	None
He continued to reverse the vehicle, ducking down to save himself from the volley of bullets, but a third bullet hit him on the left side of his waist.	None
He also realized that the left front wheel of the car was punctured.	None
He, therefore, locked all four doors of the car by means of the central locking switch and, pretending to be dead, lay down on the drivers seat.	None
At this time, he heard an explosion near the car.	None
A little while later, the two terrorists came near his car and tried to open its doors but they were unable to do so as the doors were locked.	None
After some time, he saw them from the rear windscreen of the car near the SBI office behind him.	None
His car was standing on the road in a slanting position but there was enough space on both sides for vehicles to pass.	None
As the two terrorists approached High Rise Building, they took cover behind bushes abutting that building.	None
At the same time, Phad saw a police vehicle approaching his vehicle from behind, i.e., from the side of the SBI office on Badruddin Tayabji Road.	None
As soon as the police vehicle came close to the two persons hiding in the bushes, they started firing indiscriminately at the police vehicle.	None
At the same time, the shorter fellow seemed to have sustained a bullet injury, probably from the firing from the police vehicle.	None
His gun fell down.	None
The butka, however, picked up the gun and resumed firing at the police vehicle.	None
Firing from the police vehicle stopped, and the taller man went to the vehicle and opened its right front door, pulling the driver on to the road.	None
He also pulled down another person from the vehicles middle seat.	None
The butka fellow went to the left side of the vehicle and pulled down the person sitting on the left front seat.	None
The lamboo fellow occupied the drivers seat and the butka took the front left seat.	None
Phad stated before the court that he had witnessed the above incident from a distance of about one hundred and fifty (150) feet.	None
The police vehicle thus taken over by the two terrorists proceeded towards Mahapalika Road.	None
Apprehending danger from those two persons, Phad pretended to be dead and continued lying in his vehicle.	None
That vehicle crossed Phads vehicle and went towards Mahapalika Road.	None
It was a Qualis vehicle.	None
Phad stated before the court that as a result of the injuries sustained by him he lost the ring finger on his right hand and two other fingers were not functioning properly.	None
He was no longer able to drive auto vehicles.	None
Phad gave a description to the court of the two persons whom he had seen firing on Badruddin Tayabji Road.	None
The lamboo was six (6) feet in height, of fair complexion, and was aged about twentytwo to twentyfive (2225) years.	None
The butka was five feet three inches (5 3) inches in height, of fair complexion and strongly built.	None
Phad said he could identify both of them and added that one of them was present in court, identifying the appellant as the butka.	None
He further said that he had identified the appellant in the identification parade on December 27, 2008.	None
He had identified the appellant from amongst seven (7) persons put in line with him.	None
SEO, Vichare was conducting the test identification parade.	None
He then identified the lamboo from his photograph (Article 61) and stated that earlier he had identified his dead body at the JJ mortuary from amongst ten (10) dead bodies.	None
In crossexamination Phad said that as he approached Mahapalika Road he had seen a police vehicle parked near the busstop on Mahapalika Road and had also seen the two terrorists firing on the police officers standing near the vehicle.	None
Bhushan Ashok Gagrani, who was examined as PW140, stated before the court that he called Phad between 11.30 and 11.45 PM, to bring the car to his residence at Yashodhan Building and take him to Mantralaya.	None
When the car did not come, he again called Phad	None
but he did not turn up.	None
Therefore, Gagrani went to Mantralaya in his personal vehicle.	None
At about 12.15 AM he tried to contact Phad once again.	None
This time, he got a response from the driver who told him that he had been fired at in the car that the car was stranded in the vicinity of Rang Bhavan and that he was lying injured inside it.	None
Gagrani then tried to contact the police control room but could not get through as the number was continuously engaged.	None
He then contacted the Superintendent of GT Hospital and requested him to provide help to Phad.	None
After an hour he was informed that Phad had been admitted to the hospital with bullet injuries.	None
All the phone calls made by Gagrani from his mobile phone to the mobile phone of Phad and to the hospital were independently established from the mobile phones records.	None
Arun Dada Jadhav (PW136) is a very special witness.	None
He was in the extraordinary position of actually traveling with the two terrorists, lying badly injured in the back side of the Qualis vehicle that the terrorists had hijacked after killing three (3) senior police officers and three (3) policemen on Badruddin Tayabji Road.	None
In the time that Additional Commissioner of Police Date (PW118) was engaged in the encounter with the terrorists on the sixth floor landing of the New Cama Hospital Building, a number of senior officers and policemen had gathered at the back of the hospital.	None
At that time, an injured policeman emerged from the back of the hospital.	None
He told the assembled officers that Date and some other police officers were lying injured on the higher floors of the hospital.	None
Thereupon, Kamate, Additional Commissioner of Police (East Region), Karkare, Joint Commissioner of Police (ATS) and Salaskar, Senior Police Inspector, decided to go to the front gate of Cama Hospital, anticipating that the terrorists would go out from that side.	None
They took a Qualis police jeep of Pydhonie Division that was standing there.	None
Salaskar took the drivers seat, Kamate occupied the front left seat and Karkare sat on the middle seat of the vehicle.	None
Jadhav, who was attached to the AntiExtortion Cell of which Salaskar was the chief, sat in the extreme rear of the vehicle.	None

As they proceeded on Badruddin Tayabji Road towards the SBI office, a message was received on wireless that the two terrorists were hiding on Rang Bhavan Lane near a red vehicle.	None
Rang Bhavan Lane begins from the SBI office.	None

Jadhav told the court that there were bushes on the right side of the road, about five to five and a half (55.5) feet in height.	None
As the Qualis came near the bushes, it was greeted by a burst of gunfire.	None
Jadhav looked out from the vehicles window and saw one lamboo and one butka firing at their vehicle with AK47 rifles.	None
Jadhav, Karkare, Kamate and Salaskar also fired at the lamboo and the butka from the windows of the vehicle.	None
Jadhav sustained bullet injuries on his right elbow and left shoulder.	None
Because of the injuries, the carbine fell from his hands on the vehicles floor.	None
The terrorists continued to fire at them.	None
By now, all the policemen had suffered gunshots and were injured.	None
Jadhav was unable to pick up his carbine.	None
After some time, the firing stopped and the lamboo tried to open the vehicles rear side door.	None
However, the door did not open.	None
Jadhav tried to pick up his weapon once again but could not.	None
The driver Bhosale was also badly injured and he had fallen down on Jadhav.	None
Yogesh Patil and Jaywant Patil were also unable to move.	None
Realising that it was not possible for him to retaliate, Jadhav pretended to be dead.	None
At this time he heard a door of their vehicle opening and also heard the noise of the vehicle starting.	None
He realised that the vehicle was being driven, and he then saw that the drivers seat was occupied by the lamboo.	None
Karkare, Salaskar and Kamate were no longer in the vehicle.	None
At the metro junction, Jadhav heard the sound of firing but he continued pretending to be dead.	None
He realised that one of the vehicles wheels was punctured.	None
After some time, he also realised that even the tube and tyre had come off the punctured wheel.	None
He could sense this as he was himself an experienced driver.	None
The vehicle stopped on the road behind the Vidhan Bhavan.	None
There was more firing and then he saw the two terrorists leaving the Qualis and going to a car that had stopped.	None
They left in the other car, which looked like a Honda City.	None
He could see them clearly in the street light.	None
After the terrorists had left, Jadhav informed the Police Control Room on the vehicles wireless that the two terrorists had run away in a car and that he was lying injured in the vehicle of Pydhonie division (Able) in front of the State Bank of Mysore.	None
He was rescued by a team of policemen including Amrute, Senior Police Inspector (PW137).	None

THE SKODA ROBBERY Sharan Arasa (PW144), Samit Vijay Ajgaonkar (PW147) and his wife Megha were the three occupants of the white Skoda car that Kasab and Abu Ismail snatched at gunpoint, and which Arun Dada Jadhav (PW136), lying in the back seat of the police Qualis, had thought to be a white Honda City car.	None
Arasa and Ajgaonkar had a common friend Siddharth Umashankar (PW238) who worked as Sales Manager in Oberoi Hotel.	None
When the two terrorists, namely Abdul Rehman (Chhota) and Fahadullah, entered Oberoi Hotel and started shooting there, Umashankar, along with other guests and staff members, escaped through the exit door in the lobby area.	None
They went to Inox multiplex, which is a few minutes walking distance from the Oberoi.	None
When Ajgaonkar called him on the telephone, Umashankar asked him to come to Inox and take him away from there.	None
Ajgaonkar contacted Arasa and asked him to come with his car so that they could go to Inox to fetch Umashankar.	None
Thus, Arasa took the Skoda Car (of which his father was the registered owner) and came to Ajgaonkars house at Mahim.	None
From Mahim they proceeded to Inox with Arasa driving, Ajgaonkar occupying the front left seat and his wife Megha sitting in the back.	None
They were going to rescue Umashankar but they themselves had a brush with death when they came across the two terrorists facetoface.	None
They reached Rajani Patel Road, Nariman Point, at about 00.15 hours on November 27, 2008.	None
They saw a Qualis police vehicle approaching them from the opposite direction.	None
When the Qualis was about sixty (60) feet away, someone from the police vehicle shouted at them to stop.	None
Simultaneously, a shot was fired in the air from that vehicle.	None
The Qualis stopped and two persons got down from it and approached their car.	None
The person who had got out from the left side of the police vehicle came in front of their car.	None
He asked Arasa to get out of the vehicle.	None
The other person, who had been driving the Qualis, pulled Arasa out of the Skoda car, holding him by his collar.	None
In the meantime, Samit and Megha had already left the car and were sitting on the footpath.	None
As Arasa got out of the car, he realised that he was carrying the key.	None
He, therefore, immediately threw the key away.	None
The person who had come out of the Qualis from the left side was shorter than the other person.	None
Arasa identified the appellant in court as the same short person who had come to him and asked for the cars key.	None
When Arasa had thrown away the key, it had landed near the cars rear right wheel.	None
Arasa picked up the key and gave it to the appellant.	None
The two men drove away in the car the appellant sat in the front left seat and his partner drove the car.	None
Let us now see the description of the occurrence by Ajgaonkar.	None
He stated in his deposition before the court that, when the Qualis stopped, two persons got down from it and approached their car.	None
One of them was taller and the other was shorter.	None
He identified the appellant as the shorter person who approached their car along with his associate who was taller than him.	None
The taller man approached Arasa while the appellant stood in front of the car.	None
The appellant ordered them to get out of the car (Gadi se bahar aao).	None
The taller fellow pulled Arasa out by his collar.	None
In the meantime, Ajgaonkar and his wife got down from the car and went to the footpath on the left side of the car.	None
The taller fellow occupied the drivers seat and the appellant sat on the front left seat.	None
The taller fellow, however, could not find the car keys and, hence, the appellant got down from the car and demanded the key from Arasa.	None
Arasa picked up the key which he had thrown near the car and gave it to the appellant.	None
Thereafter, both of them drove away in the Skoda car.	None
The terrorists proceeded towards Inox theatre.	None
Arasa further told the court that, at about 300 PM on November 27, 2008, he received a phone call from PSI Zende (PW148) of Marine Drive police station, asking him to come to the police station.	None
Accordingly, he went and reached there at about 345 PM.	None
He was taken to the spot from where the car was taken from him.	None
A Panchnama was drawn up by the police.	None
He was finally shown his vehicle on December 25, 2008, in the premises of the office of DCB CID.	None
There was a bullet hole on the right front door.	None
The car was badly damaged on the right side.	None
He told the court that the car was in proper condition when it was snatched away from his custody.	None
As seen above, both Arasa and Ajgaonkar identified the appellant in court.	None
Both said that they had earlier identified him in the test identification parade.	None
Arasa was one of the witnesses in the test identification parade held on December 28, 2008, and Ajgaonkar on January 14, 2009.	None

VINOLI CHOWPATY	None
For this part of the case the prosecution has examined ten (10) witnesses.	None
Leaving aside two (2) panch witnesses and a formal police witness, there are seven (7) police witnesses of whom three (3) are members of the team that overpowered Kasab and Abu Ismail and took them in custody (one of them is injured), two (2) reached the spot after Kasab was apprehended and had taken him and Abu Ismail to hospital, one (1) maintained the police logs and the last secured the area after the incident.	None
VINOLI CHOWATY ONE DEAD, ONE INJURED Kasab and Abu Ismail along with eight (8) others (the dead accused) were seen landing on the shore of Mumbai on November 26, 2008, between 9.15 and 9.30 PM.	None
Kasab and Abu Ismail snatched the Skoda car near Vidhan Sabha around 12.15 AM on November 27.	None
They came to Mumbai armed to the teeth they had the great advantage of complete surprise and were also aided by a lot of luck.	None
They were thus able to have a free run for over three (3) hours, killing innocent people and policemen at will.	None
However, their run would soon come to end as a team of policemen were waiting, determined to stop them, caring little for their own lives.	None
Abu Ismail was killed in their last encounter with a police team, but Kasab was taken alive in custody.	None
We propose to examine here three (3) witnesses who were members of the police team that stopped Kasab and Abu Ismail travelling in the stolen Skoda car and took them in custody.	None
Bhaskar Dattatray Kadam (PW1) was a SubInspector of Police attached to DB Marg Police Station.	None
On November 26, 2008, at about 22.00 hours, Senior Police Inspector Nagappa Mali told him that terrorists had attacked some parts of South Mumbai and directed him to go to Girgaon (Vinoli) Chowpaty along with members of the Crime Detection Branch and to do a nakabandi there by putting up barricades.	None
As directed by Mali, Kadam proceeded to Vinoli Chowpaty accompanied by six (6) members of the Detection Branch.	None
On reaching there, he found API Hemant Bavthankar (PW3), Peter Mobile Operator Sanjay Patil, Peter Mobile Driver Chandrakant Kamble, Girgaon Chowpaty Beat Incharge ASI Pawar, ASI Kochale, Head Constable Chavan, PN Naik and some other policemen already present there and barricades already put up.	None
Kadam and the members of the Detection Branch joined the police team already present there.	None
After some time, API Govilkar (PW2 injured) and ASI Tukaram Ombale (killed), along with some other policemen, also arrived at the nakabandi.	None
The police team was receiving messages regularly through wireless on the Peter Mobile Van.	None
They received a message that two terrorists were proceeding towards Chowpaty from Vidhan Bhawan via Marine Drive in a Skoda car.	None
At about 00.30 hours they spotted a Skoda car on Marine Drive coming from South Bombay towards Chowpaty.	None
Having been alerted in regard to the Skoda, all the policemen, including Kadam, signalled to the driver to stop the car.	None
The car stopped at a distance of about fifty (50) feet from the barricades.	None
The police team shouted to tell the driver that there was a nakabandi and they would check the car.	None
They asked the driver to put off the head lights and to put on the inside lights of the car.	None
Instead of following these directions, the driver of the car did just the opposite.	None
Not only were the head lights kept on but the wipers and the water spray on the windscreen were also switched on.	None
Therefore, it became difficult to see anything inside the car.	None
Then, in a bid to escape, the driver tried to take a uturn just before the barricades.	None
However, the car could not climb over the road divider it dashed against it and stopped.	None
Kadam and six (6) other policemen rushed towards the car and surrounded it.	None
The driver and the other person who was sitting on the front left seat raised their hands pretending surrender but, when Kadam approached the driver, he started firing at him through the lowered window.	None
Kadam fired back from his service revolver.	None
At that time Kadam was about ten to twelve (1012) feet from the driver of the car.	None
Kadam told the court that he shot the driver of the Skoda car and injured him.	None
The other occupant of the Skoda car, who was sitting on the front left seat, opened the door on his side and got out of the car.	None
While getting out, he deliberately fell on the road.	None
ASI Tukaram Ombale and API Sanjay Govilkar were proceeding towards the cars front left door.	None
The person who had got out of the car from the front left door started firing at Tukaram Ombale with an AK47 rifle.	None
Even as he was being fired at, Tukaram Ombale threw himself bodily upon his assailant.	None
Tukaram Ombale and Govilkar were injured by shots from the AK47 rifle.	None
Other members of Ombales and Govilkars team started hitting the assailant with lathis.	None
They succeeded in disarming him.	None
His AK47 rifle was snatched away from him by policemen and he was taken into custody.	None
Within ten (10) minutes of this occurrence, Senior PI Mali, PI Sawant (PW31), PI Surulkar, API Yadav, API Gawade (PW4), PSI Gaikwad (PW24) and PSI Warang (PW27) reached the spot.	None

It needs to be clarified here that Article 12, the AK47 rifle which was identified by Kadam (PW1), Govilkar (PW2) and Bavthankar (PW3) as having been recovered from the leg space below the drivers seat of the Skoda car actually belonged to the slain police officer Ashok Kamte, Additional Police Commissioner.	None
Abu Ismail evidently picked it up while switching from the Qualis to the Skoda, leaving his own AK47 rifle in the damaged Qualis.	None
Arun Balkrishna Jande (PW7) who was working at Naigaon Police Armoury at the relevant time deposed before the court that Article 12, the AK47 rifle and the magazine were issued to Ashok Kamte, Additional Commissioner of Police on August 4, 2008.	None
He identified Article 12, the AK47 rifle from the number on its butt (94) and the body (LY8860) on the basis of the entry (Ext. no. 76) made in the register maintained in the armoury.	None
The empty magazine with it also bore the same number.	None
On the other hand the AK47 rifle along with a magazine (labeled Articles 427 and 428 respectively) that was recovered from the damaged Qualis police vehicle under seizure Panchnama (Ext. no. 529) belonged to Abu Ismail and he had carried it with him from Pakistan.	None
This becomes clear from the ballistic analysis of the bullets recovered from dead bodies which shows that one Ashrafali, who was killed at CST and Ashok Kamte, who was killed in the Qualis police vehicle were hit by bullets fired from the AK47 rifle, Article 427.This is also in conformity with what the appellant stated in his confession before the magistrate that as they left the Qualis police vehicle, Abu Ismail left behind his AK47, the magazines of which had emptied by then and picked up the AK47 of one of the officers lying dead in the vehicle.	None
VILE PARLE BLAST TWO DEAD, THREE INJURED Before concluding the narration of crimes directly committed by Kasab in the company of Abu Ismail, we must take note of another event.	None
A taxi bearing registration number MH01G7792 was blown up by a bomb blast on western express highway, Vile Parle (East), near Swan City Club at slightly after 1045 PM on November 26, 2008.	None
The explosion destroyed the vehicle and instantly killed its two occupants (the driver and a passenger).	None
The explosion was witnessed by Shyamsunder Rambharat Choudhary (PW171), Balkrushna Ramchandra Bare (PW490) and Sheldon Alman (PW491).	None
As a result of the explosion, Choudhary suffered a bleeding injury on his right shoulder, Bare sustained injuries on his face below the eyelid, and on the forehead, nose and ear, and Alman on his left hand.	None
Choudhary and Bare were admitted as indoor patients and treated at Cooper Hospital, and Alman at Holy Spirit Hospital.	None
The two occupants of the taxi, i.e., the driver and the passenger, who lost their lives in the explosion, were Umar Shaikh and Laxminarayan Goyal respectively.	None
In the narration of this painful and gory tale, one comes across brutal and mindless killings at every step but there are some killings, like the present one, that stand out as especially sorrowful.	None
Shaikh was a taxi driver eking out a livelihood by plying a taxi of which he was not even the owner, and Goyal was a lawyer from Hyderabad who had come to Mumbai in connection with some professional work.	None
The only fault of the taxi driver was that he was hired by the two messengers of death to carry them from Badhwar Park to CST and of the passenger that on that chaotic night in Mumbai, when death seemed to be lurking around every corner, he had thought that a taxi would be a safer mode of transport than the local trains.	None
As noted above, Goyal had come to Mumbai in connection with some professional work and he was due to go back to Hyderabad by a train leaving CST in the evening of November 26, 2008.	None
He reached CST but missed the train.	None
His sisterinlaw Usha Sharad Chaudhary (PW168) lived in Mumbai at Charkop, Kandivali (W).	None
Goyal called her from his mobile phone to tell her that there was some incident of firings at CST and he had missed his train and he was coming back to her place.	None
On account of the city being under terrorist attack, she asked him not to travel by any local train but to take a taxi.	None
After five (5) minutes, he called her again to tell her that he had boarded a taxi and left CST.	None
Usha Sharad Chaudhary was quite anxious and called Goyal from her mobile phone again at about 1030 PM.	None
He told her that he had reached Dadar.	None
At about 1145 PM, Usha Sharad Chaudhary received a phone call from Goyals daughter Diksha, who stayed at Walkeshwar, Mumbai, saying that she had last spoken to her father at about 1045 PM and thereafter her fathers phone was not reachable.	None
That was the last anyone spoke to or heard from Goyal.	None
His mutilated body was later found at Cooper Hospital.	None
Umar Sheikh, too, while carrying Goyal in his taxi, was called by his friend Irshad Ahmed Shaikh (PW169) on his mobile at about 1000 PM on November 26, 2008.	None
Irshad had given his driving licence for renewal to Umar (the deceased) and he was enquiring whether it had been renewed.	None
Umar told him that the friend to whom he had given the licence for renewal had not brought it back and added that in view of all the disturbances in the city it was good that he (Irshad Ahmed Shaikh) would not be driving on that night.	None
At this Irshad, asked him why, in that case, was he proceeding to Kandivali with a passenger in his taxi?	None
Umar told him that it was only because the passenger seemed to be in trouble and he had made a very earnest request to take him to Kandivali by any means.	None
In the morning of November 27, 2008, Irshad Shaikh learnt from TV news that there had been a bomb blast in a taxi at Vile Parle.	None
He and some friends went in search of Umar Shaikh and found his dead body at Coroners Court at Cooper Hospital.	None
BEYOND VINOLI	None
The above is a broad account of the havoc wrought by Kasab and Abu Ismail over a period of slightly more than three (3) hours, beginning with their arrival at Badhwar Park and ending with their being apprehended at Vinoli Chowpaty.	None
It must, however, be made clear that the above account is based only on part of the ocular evidence led by the prosecution before the trial court.	None
Besides the depositions referred to above, the prosecution has an enormous volume of other evidence such as articles recovered and seized from places through which the two terrorists passed, and the places where they stopped the vehicles they used until they were finally caught medical and forensic reports, CCTV recordings, phone call records, Station Diary entries, police logs, etc.	None
We see no reason, however, to refer to all that evidence since, on the basis of the ocular evidence discussed above alone, we have no doubt that the appellant, personally and jointly with Abu Ismail, is directly responsible for killing at least seventytwo (72) people.	None
and causing injuries of various kinds to one hundred and thirty (130) people All the witnesses discussed above (except those relating to the Vile Parle and Mazgaon Taxi blasts) had a life and death encounter with the appellant and his associate, Abu Ismail (deceased accused no.1), at close quarters.	None
The physical appearance of the two terrorists was etched on their minds.	None
All the witnesses gave a detailed description of the two terrorists to the court.	None
They described them by their complexion, age, bodybuilt and height, stating that one of them was tall and the other was short.	None
All of them identified the appellant in court as the shorter of the two assailants.	None
They also identified Abu Ismail from the photograph on the fake identity card Article 61.	None
They also stated before the court that they had identified the appellant in the test identification parades held.	None
We accept their testimony without any hesitation.	None
From the forensic evidence it further appears that of the seventytwo (72) dead, at least six (6) persons fell to shots fired by the appellant.	None
We, therefore, see no difficulty whatsoever in holding him guilty of multiple murder, murder with common intention and abetment, attempt to murder with common intention and abetment, abducting in order to murder, robbery with attempt to cause death or grievous hurt, and several other allied offences under the Penal Code (IPC), committing terrorist act punishable under Section 16 of Unlawful Activities (Prevention) Act, 1967, as well as offences under the Explosives Act, 1884, Explosive Substances Act, 1908, and Arms Act, 1959.	None
Nothing will please Mr. Raju Ramachandran, senior counsel appearing for the appellant, more than stopping at this stage.	None
As a matter of fact, he made a fervent plea to segregate the case of the appellant from the other eight (8) dead accused.	Arguments of Petitioner
He urged that, for the purpose of this appeal, the court need not go into the offences committed by the eight (8) other dead terrorists who, though, arrived together with the appellant and Abu Ismail at Badhwar park, but went their separate ways from there.	Arguments of Petitioner
The learned Counsel submitted that the appellants culpability should be judged, and the commensurate punishment for him should be determined only on the basis of the offences directly attributable to him.	Arguments of Petitioner
In other words, he would like to confine the case only to acts committed by the appellant along with the dead Abu Ismail from the time the two landed at Badhwar Park until they were caught at Vinoli Chowpaty.	Arguments of Petitioner
Mr. Gopal Subramanium, learned senior advocate appearing for the State of Maharashtra, was quite shocked by the suggestion made by Mr. Ramachandran.	None
Mr. Subramanium submitted that stopping at this stage of the case would amount to shutting out the prosecution unheard.	None
Learned Counsel submitted that the offences committed by the appellant in the company of the dead Abu Ismail can never be properly appreciated in isolation.	None
The appellant and his companion, the dead Abu Ismail, were part of a closeknit team of ten (10) terrorists who arrived together on the soil of Mumbai in a highly organised way and attacked their various targets in furtherance of a common conspiracy.	None
The learned Counsel submitted that the full magnitude of the case would only be clear as the prosecution unfolds the evidence relating to conspiracy.	None
He submitted that, as the evidence relating to the other aspects of the case and the five (5) other venues of violence is set out before the court, it would become clear that a much larger and ominous conspiracy was hatched in Pakistan, the aim of which was to destabilize the country and to wage war against the Government of India.	None
It would also be clear that all ten (10) terrorists, including Kasab and Abu Ismail, who spread out from Badhwar Park in pairs, were acting in concert and in execution of the larger conspiracy.	None
Seen thus, the appellant would appear equally culpable for the carnage and other offences committed by the other terrorists of the team at different places, though admittedly he was not physically present at the venues of those crimes.	None
Mr. Subramanium submitted that the course suggested by Mr. Ramachandran would do grave injustice to the prosecution, nay to the people of the country who came under a completely unprovoked attack and suffered a war waged against them that was encouraged, monitored, and guided from minute to minute from a command post based in a foreign land.	None
We are of the view that Mr. Subramanium is clearly right.	None
The suggestion made by Mr. Ramachandran that the appellant should only be held liable for acts committed by him in the company of Abu Ismail is based on the premise that the appellant and Abu Ismail were acting independently and separately from the other terrorists who, on arriving at Mumbai, went to four different targets.	None
It is contended that though all ten (10) terrorists arrived in Mumbai together, on the same inflatable rubber dinghy, each of the five pairs into which they divided themselves must be held liable for the actions of the pair alone and not for what the other four pairs might have done, because each pair went in a different direction from the landing site.	None
The underlying assumption is that the five pairs were not connected to each other by a common conspiracy and that they were not acting in furtherance of a conspiracy that was keeping them bound together even after they had separated physically in order to execute their assigned roles under the conspiracy.	None
We find no basis for such an assumption, even in light of the prosecution evidence discussed so far.	None
Further, it would be wrong to proceed on such an assumption even without taking into account the evidence of conspiracy that the prosecution has to present with reference to the other aspects of the case and the other venues of the terrorist attack.	None
We, therefore, deem it necessary to proceed with the matter further and to examine the other venues of carnage.	None
But we propose to scrutinize the other aspects of the case and visit the other four places of terrorist violence primarily with the view to see what the prosecution has to offer by way of evidence of conspiracy and in support of the various other charges against the appellant.	None
We do not propose to discuss the evidence relating to the offences committed by the other eight (8) dead terrorists at those places in any great detail for the simple reason that, being dead, they were not on trial.	None
After landing at Badhwar Park, the appellant and Abu Ismail, the leader of the group (deceased accused no.1), went to CST by a taxi.	None
At the railway station they killed as many people as they could and then left via the footoverbridge to Badruddin Tayabji Marg.	None
They overcame any efforts by the police to stop them on the sixth floor of the Cama Hospital building, at the main front gate of the hospital and on Badruddin Tayabji Marg near Rang Bhavan Lane.	None
In the process, they killed, among many others, three (3) senior police officers and grabbed the Qualis vehicle in which they were trying to intercept the two terrorists.	None
They were unable to go very far in the Qualis as one of its wheels was destroyed in the gun fire.	None
They then commandeered another vehicle, a Skoda, from its occupants at gunpoint.	None
They were driving the Skoda on Marine Drive when they were finally caught at Vinoli Chowpaty.	None
The road on which they were travelling goes to Malabar Hill and their car was headed in that direction.	None
In his statement before the magistrate, the appellant had said that as they sat in the Skoda after seizing it from its occupants he had asked Abu Ismail where they had to go.	None
Abu Ismail said they had to go to Malabar Hill.	None
The appellant further asked where exactly in Malabar Hill, but Abu Ismail said that he would tell him on reaching Malabar Hill.	None
There is no other evidence that their destination was actually Malabar Hill.	None
It is also not clear as to where exactly they intended to go once they reached Malabar Hill or who was were their target(s) there.	None
But it is worth remembering that the Governor and the Chief Minister of Maharashtra as well as the Chief Justice of Bombay High Court all reside on Malabar Hill.	None
It is quite possible that the two desperados had anyone among them as their next target.	None
Following the appellant and Abu Ismail, Nazir Ahmad Abu Omair (deceased accused no.4) and Shoaib Abu Soheb (deceased accused no. 9) took a taxi from Badhwar Park for Leopold Caf.	None
They were followed by Abdul Rahman Bada Hajazi (deceased accused no.5) and Javed Abu Ali (deceased accused no.8) who went to Hotel Taj by taxi.	None
After them, Imran Babar Abu Aqsa (deceased accused no.2) and Nasir Abu Umar (deceased accused no.3) went to Nariman House on foot.	None
After these eight (8) men had left, the remaining two, namely, Fahadullah (deceased accused no.7) and Abdul Rahman Chhota Saqib (deceased accused no.6) sailed the rubber boat to Nariman Point from where they just walked into Hotel Oberoi.	None
Here it needs to be made clear that the nine (9) dead accused could only be known by their respective names after the appellant identified them through photographs of their dead bodies Later he also named them and referred to their respective roles in his confessional statement before the magistrate.	None
Further, the fact that the four terrorists at Hotel Taj were called Abu Soheb, Omair, Rahman and Abu Ali also comes in the evidence of Sunil Rajaram Jadhav (PW224) and Nivruti Tukaram Kadam (PW242).	None
Also, the names of the terrorists who went to Hotel Oberoi and Nariman House come through in the transcripts of their intercepted phone calls, in which they are talking with their collaborators and to which we shall advert in due course.	None
Leopold Caf eleven (11) dead and twentyeight (28) injured and the Mazgaon blast three (3) dead and nineteen (19) injured Nazir (deceased accused no.4) and Shoaib (deceased accused no.9) launched an attack on Leopold Caf with grenades and gunfire from AK47 rifles and left it within minutes, leaving behind eleven (11) dead (of whom two (2) were foreign nationals) and twentyeight (28) injured (of whom nine (9) were foreign nationals).	None
They walked to Hotel Taj, which is at a distance of about hundred (100) metres to join Abdul Rahman Bada and Javed who had gone directly to the Hotel by taxi from Badhwar Park.	None
Nazir and Shoaib were carrying two RDX bombs, one of which they had planted in the taxi they took from Badhwar Park to Leopold Caf.	None
The bomb in the taxi exploded at about 1030 PM while it was going through the Wadi Bunder Road in the Mazgaon Area of the city, killing its driver, Fulchandra Ramchandra Bind, and its two passengers, Zarina Shamsuddin Shaikh and her daughter Reema Mohammad Rabiul Shaikh (the motherinlaw and wife, respectively, of Mohammad Shaikh (PW176)) and causing injuries to nineteen (19) people on the road.	None
The other RDX bomb they planted while on way from Leopold Caf to Hotel Taj, in Gokul Wine Shop Lane behind Hotel Taj, near Gokul Restaurant in front of the State Bank of Hyderabad.	None
The bomb, however, did not explode and it was finally recovered and seized under the Panchnama Ext. no. 736.	None
Hotel Taj thirtysix (36) dead and thirty (30) injured Abdul Rahman Bada (deceased accused no.5) and Javed (deceased accused no.8), on reaching Hotel Taj, first put their RDX bomb near a tree at a distance of about fifty (50) metres from the porch of the New Taj Hotel.	None
This bomb, too, did not explode and was recovered and seized along with the bomb planted by the Leopoldteam under the Panchnama Ext. no. 736.	None
They then entered the lobby of the hotel and started firing with their AK47 rifles on burst mode.	None
Leaving the commotion behind, they went to the upper floors of the hotel using its wide winding stairs.	None
On the fifth floor of the hotel they planted the second RDX bomb, placing it under the central dome so as to cause maximum damage to the building.	None
Next, they proceeded to the sixth floor where they took Kuttalam Rajgopalan Ramamoorthy (PW184) into captivity.	None
Ramamoorthy was the nonExecutive Chairman of ING Vysya Bank After having taken and he had gone to Mumbai in connection with a board meeting of one of the companies.	None
He was staying at Hotel Taj Palace in Room no.632 on the sixth floor.	None
Abdul Rahman Bada and Javed also took four employees of the hotel as hostages, namely, Adil Rohinton Irani .	None
(PW188), Sunil Jadhav (PW224), Rajendra Bagade and Swapnil.	None
In room no.632, Abdul Rahman Bada and Javed were joined by Nazir and Shoaib, coming from Leopold Caf.	None
At about 2.15 AM (on November 27, 2008) all four terrorists came down to the fifth floor, bringing with them all five hostages, with their hands tied behind their backs, and went into room no.520.	None
While they were in that room, a call came from Adils wife on his mobile phone.	None
Adil was then held captive by the terrorists who had also taken away his mobile phone.	None
The terrorists talked to his wife menacingly and asked her to stop security forces acting against them otherwise they would not only kill Adil but wreak havoc.	None
All the while, they were engaged in a long conversation with their collaborators and handlers on a mobile phone these handlers were constantly urging them to throw grenades and to set fire to the hotel building.	None
While they were trying to build a fire by setting ablaze inflammable articles in the room like sofa(s), foam mattresses, curtains, bed sheets, etc., there was a major blast somewhere in the hotel building and heavy smoke started to fill the room.	None
When it became difficult to breathe inside the room, the four terrorists came out of the room and in that confusion the four hotel staff were able to escape through rooms window by tying up bed sheets and curtains into a rope for climbing down.	None
Ramamoorthy was unable to climb down by this rope but he too was able to escape and to reach a window from where he was finally rescued by the fire brigade personnel.	None
Having lost their hostages, the four terrorists settled down in the hotel, taking position for a longdrawn battle with security forces and continued their attempts to set fire to the hotel and to destroy it by whatever means they could.	None
They gave a tough fight to the security forces till they were finally killed on the morning of November 29, 2008.	None
The last of the four terrorists at Hotel Taj (Abdul Rahman Bada) was shot by security forces at 900 AM on November 29, 2008.	None
By that time, the four men had killed thirtysix (36) people (of whom nine (9) were foreign nationals) and caused injuries of various kinds to thirty (30) others (of whom five (5) were foreign nationals).	None
Nariman House nine (9) killed and seven (7) injured Imran Babar Abu Aqsa (deceased accused no.2) and Nasir Abu Umar (deceased accused no.3) had gone to Nariman House from Badhwar Park on foot.	None
On reaching near Nariman House they first planted an RDX bomb at the Express Petrol Pump on SBS Road, Colaba.	None
From there they proceeded to Nariman House, where they planted the second RDX bomb near the staircase on the ground (parking level area).	None
They then entered the upper floors of Nariman House without difficulty.	None
Nariman House is a six (6) storied (ground plus five) building.	None
It is a residentialcumprayer house used by Israeli people for temporary accommodation.	None
An Israeli priest called Gabriel Holtzberge lived there permanently with his wife Rivka and their two (2) year old son Moshe.	None
They had two (2) employees.	None
One was Kazi Zakir Hussain (PW239), who was provided accommodation on the ground floor, and the other was a woman called Sandra.	None
Besides these two, they had a watchman called Kesari who, however, was not present at the time of the occurrence on November 26, 2008.	None
On the date of the occurrence there were four guests, two males and two females, staying with the Holtzberge couple at Nariman House.	None
Dinner, on November 26, 2008, was over by 8.00 PM.	None
And by 9.45 PM Hussain was going down to his accommodation after he and Sandra had finished their days work.	None
On the stairs he saw a person armed with a gun standing on the landing area between the first and second floors.	None
The gunman fired a shot at Hussain but he was not hit.	None
Hussain immediately returned to the first floor where Sandra was still in the hall.	None
On entering the first floor hall, Hussain shut the door from inside.	None
Gabriel, Rivka and their four guests were at that time on the second floor.	None
Hussain and Sandra hid themselves in the store room, bolting the door from inside and putting off the lights.	None
They came out of the store room at 11.00 AM on November 27, 2008.	None
All through the night and in the morning there had been sounds of gunshots being fired from inside the building.	None
While they were trying to get out of the building, they heard the child Moshe crying on the second floor.	None
They went up and found Moshe on the second floor hall.	None
Sandra picked up the boy and brought him out with them.	None
On coming out of Nariman House they were immediately taken to Colaba Police Station.	None
See the evidence of KaziHussai Zakir n (PW239).	None
It was their exemplary courage, humanity and loyalty to their employers that saved the child Moshe from certain death at the hands of the two terrorists.	None
The Nariman House episode indeed presents a shining example of good and proper human conduct in the face of grave personal danger, but there were also many tragic killings of innocent people at Nariman House.	None
The two terrorists took Gabriel, Rivka and their guests as hostages.	None
They first tried to use them as bargaining chips to start some sort of negotiation with the Indian authorities but, when they were unable to start any negotiation and as they came under the heat of the security forces operation, they simply killed all their hostages as being expendable baggage and encumbrances in their fight against the security forces.	None
Apart from the inmates of Nariman House, two other people lost their lives in the most tragic circumstances.	None
Mohammad Salim Harharwala (PW206) lived along with his family at 73/4 Faridun Court Building, SBS Road, Colaba, which is very close to Nariman House.	None
Apprehending danger and feeling insecure at Faridun Court because of the incident of firings in Nariman House, he shifted with his family to a flat on the fourth floor of Colaba Court, which is situated in front of Nariman House.	None
This, unfortunately, turned out to be a fatal decision.	None
In the Colaba flat, he and his parents were standing near a window facing Nariman House when, at about 1030 PM, his parents were hit by bullets fired directly from Nariman House.	None
They were taken to ST Georges hospital where they were declared dead.	None
From Nariman House the terrorists made random firings in all directions and threw hand grenades at adjoining buildings, roads and lanes that resulted in many injuries.	None
There is another aspect of the Nariman House episode to which we shall advert in greater detail in the latter part of the judgment.	None
From Nariman House the two terrorists, Imran Babar in particular, were in regular contact on the mobile phone with their handlers and corroborators across the border.	None
At one stage, the controllers even tried to use one of their hostages, Norma Shvarzblat Robinovich (a Mexican citizen, later killed), as an intermediary in an attempt to start some sort of negotiation with the Indian authorities.	None
The collaborators tried to tutor her as to what she should speak to the Indian authorities on the telephone.	None
She was told not to disclose her own position or the position of her captors inside the house and further not to disclose the number of hostages taken by them but to persuade the Indian authorities to stop the operation by the security forces and to negotiate with her captors in order to save the lives of the hostages.	None
Apart from the collaborators and handlers, Imran Babar also engaged in dialogues with India TV, a popular news channel in the country, and with one Levi from the US who apparently intervened as a selfstyled mediator to try and save the lives of the Jewish hostages.	None
The two terrorists holed up in Nariman House, Imran Babar Abu Aqsa and Nasir Abu Umar, were finally killed by security forces in the night of November 28, 2008.	None
But, by then, they had been able to kill nine (9) people (of whom five (5) were foreign nationals) and injure seven (7) people.	None
Hotel Oberoi thirtyfive (35) dead twentyfour (24) injured.	None
Fahadullah (deceased accused no.7) and Abdul Rahman Chhota Saqib (deceased accused no.6) entered Hotel Oberoi at about 2155 hours on November 26, 2008 and started burst firing in the hotel lobby.	None
In the CCTV recording one can clearly see a hotelstaff opening a door, coming out and going around the reception desk.	None
He gets hit by shots fired by the two terrorists and slumps down to the floor.	None
They next went to Tiffin Restaurant, situated in the main lobby of the Hotel, and fired indiscriminately from their AK47 rifles.	None
The hotel staff in Kandhar Restaurant, situated on the mezzanine floor, heard and saw them firing in Tiffin Restaurant.	None
At that time there were fifty to sixty (5060) guests in Kandhar Restaurant.	None
The staff members closed the door of Kandhar Restaurant and bolted it from inside and started taking out the guests from the rear (service) door.	None
From Tiffin Restaurant the two terrorists proceeded towards Kandhar Restaurant but they found the restaurants entrance door locked from inside.	None
They fired at the closed doors.	None
One of the shots pierced through the glass pane and hit Dinaj Sharma, one of the hotel staff, on her right forearm.	None
They eventually succeeded in breaking open the door and entering Kandhar Restaurant but by that time, fortunately, all the guests in the restaurant had been evacuated and the two terrorists found only two hotel employees, namely Jorden and Pradeep Rammurthy Bengalorkar (PW212).	None
They threatened them that they would kill them if they tried to run away.	None
Then they asked Bengalorkar to pour liquor on the tables and other items of furniture from the bottles in the bar counter and handed a lighter to Jorden, telling him to set fire to the furniture soaked with liquor.	None
The lighter did not work and they asked Jorden to make the fire with matchsticks.	None
Jorden took out a matchbox from his pocket and tried to set fire to the table cloth.	None
The poor fellow was so nervous that he was unable to start the fire but, in the process, he burnt his own hands.	None
As he was wringing his hands and crying that his hands were burnt, one of the two terrorists, evidently annoyed at his lack of efficiency as an arsonist, fired a burst of bullets, killing him on the spot.	None
They then asked Bengalorkar to set the furniture on fire.	None
He somehow succeeded in setting fire to a table.	None
The terrorists then asked him to take them to the floor where the hotels VIP guests were staying.	None
Bengalorkar entered the lift, as bidden by the terrorists, but as their attention was momentarily diverted in throwing hand grenades he quickly pressed the down button of the lift.	None
The lift door thus closed and the lift started descending even as the terrorists fired at its closed door.	None
Bengalorkar thus gave the slip to the terrorists and saved himself by his presence of mind.	None
Fahadullah and Abdul Rahman Chhota then went to the upper floors of the hotel in search of any VIP guests staying there.	None
They were unable to find any but they got holed up there and fought the security forces till they were finally killed at about 7.00 AM on November 28, 2008.	None
A complete and ocular account of the final encounter of the two terrorists with the National Security Guard (NSG) Commando may be seen in the evidence of Rajesh Ganpat Kadam (PW215) who was the Assistant Chief Security Officer, Hotel Oberoi, and who was accompanying the NSG Commandos headed by Colonel Rathi and Lt. Colonel Sharma in the final encounter with the terrorists.	None
Before Fahadullah and Abdul Rahman Chhota were killed, they had left behind thirtyfive (35) people as dead (of whom ten (10) were foreign nationals) and twentyfour 24 injured (of whom seven (7) were foreign nationals).	None
